Important Foreign Telegrams

The United States, Following England, 64

Recognizes New Spain

Rumors of Naval Mutiny Untrue

Reuter's, Washington, 22nd - The US government has recognized the Spanish Republic.

Reuter's, London, 22nd - British Foreign Secretary Henderson stated in the House of Commons today that the governments of the overseas autonomous territories fully and formally approved the resolution to recognize the new Spanish government.

Reuter's, Madrid, 22nd - The crews of two destroyers and the Sevizia warship in the port of Cadiz have mutinied. Details are unknown. However, it is heard that the mutineers have surrendered and are now being held in prisons on shore. It is widely believed that the mutiny was incited by the Communist Party. Another telegram states that the reports of a naval mutiny in the port of Cadiz are clearly untrue. According to the latest news, after the fleet arrived in Cadiz, the sailors went ashore to demonstrate for the Republican Party and tore up the royal flags of many homes. There were no other actions.

Reuter's, Paris, 23rd - A reporter from a French newspaper stationed in Madrid met with Prime Minister Zamora, who reportedly said that Spain may not prosecute Alfonso's crimes, but the issue will be decided by the elected parliament.

National News Agency, Madrid, 23rd - The current frontrunners for the new president of the Spanish Republic are Dr. Marañón and Professor Ramón. Current Prime Minister Dr. Zamora does not seem willing to abandon his active political career and is unlikely to accept the presidential nomination.

Three-Nation Naval Treaty 65

France Has New Proposals

National News Agency, London, 22nd - Today, the French Ambassador to the United Kingdom sent a note to British Foreign Secretary Henderson containing new proposals from the French government regarding the Three-Nation Naval Treaty. The British Foreign Secretary immediately announced that he would forward the note to Rome for consideration by the Italian government. All matters related to the proposals in the drafting committee have been temporarily suspended pending the outcome of the consultations among the three nations. The new French proposals were decided yesterday after a meeting between the French Prime Minister, the two ministers of the navy, and expert Masri. If Britain and Italy can agree, the biggest difficulty in the drafting meeting can be resolved.

Japan-Russia Fisheries Dispute 66

Japan Disappointed with Russian Reply

Reuter's, Tokyo, 23rd - The Japan-Russia fisheries dispute has encountered an unexpected setback. The Soviet Union only intends to accept about one-third of the proposals recently put forward by the Japanese authorities. The departure of Japanese fishing boats to Russian waters must now be postponed. Although the Russian reply arrived here last night, the contents have not yet been released by the authorities. The authorities are clearly very disappointed and expect to send instructions to the Japanese ambassador to Russia to negotiate with the Russian authorities again. Although the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is confident that it can prevent Japanese fishing boats from sailing to Russian waters before the negotiations are concluded, it is feared that the boats may not be willing to sit idly by and suffer losses, miss the fishing season, and take the risk of sailing out.

Bloodshed Among Burmese Civilians 67

National News Agency, Bombay, 22nd - Five hundred rebel civilians in the Taityo Myaing region of Burma attacked the local police, but after a long period of fierce fighting, the rebels were finally repelled. Twenty-five people were killed and countless were injured.

Unrest in Portuguese Territory Continues 68

The Rebel Party Firmly Holds Madeira Island

Preparing for a Decisive Battle with Government Forces

National News, Lisbon, 23rd - The rebels on Madeira Island are holding firm and refusing to surrender. They have issued a radio broadcast declaring their determination to fight the Lisbon troops to the death. A bloody battle is expected in the coming days. The commander of the government forces may send troops to land on the north end of the island. Most of the rebels are stationed there, guarding the key passes in the mountains, and have built defensive works along Funchal and other coastal passes, installing six-inch heavy guns and Vickers guns for protection. On the government forces' side, warships and 8,000 marines transferred from the Azores, as well as armed fishing boats, are anchored near the island. Bombardment may begin today. According to news from Bolama, the revolutionary fervor has now spread to Portuguese Guinea in Africa, where the civilian and military governors have been imprisoned and power has been seized by the rebel party.

Revolution Spreads in Honduras 69

Reuter's, New York, 22nd - The revolution in the Republic of Honduras in Central America is spreading and shows no signs of abating. According to news received today from the capital of Honduras, the rebel party and government troops clashed on the north coast. Twenty-nine rebels were killed and few government troops were killed or wounded.

British House of Commons Questions China Affairs 70

Consular Jurisdiction Negotiations are in Progress

Efforts to Proceed with the Kailuan Issue

Reuter's, London, 22nd - British Foreign Secretary Henderson stated in the House of Commons this afternoon that the current negotiations between China and Britain are about consular jurisdiction. If the negotiations are successful, as he hopes, a treaty can be signed, and before the treaty is signed, the House of Commons will be given an opportunity for debate as usual. Conservative Party member Miller asked whether the future of Shanghai was included in the negotiations. The Foreign Secretary replied that he was paying attention to the matter, but it was not convenient to speak at the moment. Miller said that before negotiating with a government that cannot protect its own people, let alone British people, the House of Commons should know something. The Foreign Secretary replied that this was another matter. A Labor Party member asked if this was another case of secret diplomacy, but the Foreign Secretary did not answer. Conservative Party member Lampson asked whether the current negotiations were based on the report published by the Consular Jurisdiction Committee several years ago. The Foreign Secretary replied that this question should be answered later. The Foreign Secretary also said that news had come from China that the British Ambassador and Chinese Foreign Minister Wang asked about the imminent conclusion of the consular jurisdiction agreement, but the Ministry of Foreign Affairs knew nothing about it. All that is known is that the issue is currently in progress.

Reuter's, London, 22nd - Conservative Party member Samuel asked in the House of Commons this afternoon what steps the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is taking to ensure that the interests of the British in the Kailuan Mining Bureau can receive fair treatment in terms of transportation on the Beining Railway. Foreign Secretary Henderson replied that Ambassador Lampson has been in close contact with the Kailuan Management Office and has negotiated with the Chinese authorities. He will continue to work hard to help resolve this issue.

French Cash Shipped to the US in Batches 71

Reuter's, New York, 23rd - For the past four years, no French cash has been shipped to the United States, but yesterday the French ship Paris brought the first batch of cash, valued at US$3.5 million. Two more batches, worth a total of US$13 million, have been arranged. France is shipping gold to the US as a result of the recent decrease in shipping costs between Havre and New York.

Unprecedented 72

Japanese Dyeing and Weaving Industry Hunger Strike

Started to Protest Dismissal of Workers

Reuter's, Tokyo, 23rd - About 200 male workers at a Japanese dyeing and weaving company went on a hunger strike on Tuesday to protest the company's dismissal of a worker. They have locked themselves in a warehouse, saying they will not eat until the company reinstates the dismissed worker. The company's directors and those who sympathize with the hunger strikers have brought food, but the strikers are determined not to eat anything but water. About 100 female workers have gone on strike to show their sympathy for the hunger strikers. Other labor unions are also rising to support them. The public here is paying close attention to this unprecedented strike.

German Murderer Sentenced to Death 73

Appears Gentle but Harboring Treachery

Countless Women Have Suffered

National News, Dosdotofu, 22nd - The murderous demon Peter Goten has been sentenced to death. (The following is from the Telegraph Agency) To date, four young girls, four young women, and one man have died at the hands of this demon, and seven have narrowly escaped. He enticed women to the suburbs with sweet words, then killed them and left with a smile, disappearing without a trace. This was his usual method of killing. Although the police conducted a thorough search, they found no clues, so that for a time the women of the city dared not go out after dusk. He even played tricks, writing to the police and mocking their incompetence. It was not until his sins were full that he was finally arrested last May. The clue to his arrest came from the mother of a murdered girl, Maria, a peasant woman, who received a letter from him, sensed something was wrong, and boldly threw herself into the net, secretly informing the police in advance to set up a tight ambush, so that he could be captured. In summary, his appearance should have been ferocious and terrifying, but it was not. Everyone who knew him usually called him a gentle and honest gentleman. When the case was solved, everyone was shocked. He had been imprisoned for seventeen years for accumulated theft cases. After his release from prison, he was secretive, did not associate with bad people, paid his taxes on time, worked diligently, had a graceful demeanor, and spoke very gently, so that many women were deceived by him. In prison, he still liked to groom himself, and the jailers were also amazed. When interrogated by the police, he confessed that his motive for killing was nothing more than an impulse to kill as a kind of game, and there was no other intention.

Important News

Third Session of the Aviation Conference 74

The National Aviation Conference held its third session at 9:00 AM on the 23rd. Sixty-eight members attended. Chairman Zhang Hui presided over the meeting. First, the secretary-general read the resolutions of the previous session. Then, the report of the Third Review Committee was discussed. The results are as follows:

Regarding National Defense Aviation Matters, a total of 11 proposals: (A) Proposal 1, regarding the capital's air defense problem, attention should be paid to construction in the capital first; Proposal 5, establish an air defense organization; (Review Comments) The above two proposals are both about air defense problems and should both be established. Item 2 of the method in Proposal 1 is proposed to be amended to "However, the basement should have equipment to prevent poisonous gas and liquids, and use neutralizers or...temporary breathing." Item 5 should be completely deleted. In peacetime, the methods of Proposal 5 are intended to be undertaken separately by the competent authorities, planning and implementation, and a air defense headquarters will be established to govern them during wartime. Please discuss and decide by the conference. (Resolution) Passed. (B) Proposal 2, air forces should be established quickly in the frontier provinces and regions; Proposal 11, develop aviation in the Northwest; (Review Comments) The above two proposals are of the same nature and are proposed to be merged and changed to "Develop aviation in the frontier regions." The reason is taken from Proposal 11, and the method is also taken from Proposal 11, changed to "The competent authority shall formulate the development of aviation in various frontier regions." Please decide by the conference whether it is appropriate. (Resolution) The conference will submit it to the Ministry of Military Affairs and then submit it to the National Government to order the competent authority to plan and handle it. (C) Proposal 4, expand naval aviation to consolidate coastal defense; Proposal 6, military aviation organizations should organize an aviation national defense conference to review the national aviation national defense plan in detail; Proposal 8, determine prohibited airspace; Proposal 9, stipulate prohibited airspace; Proposal 10, divide the national aviation area to strengthen national defense; (Review Comments) The above five proposals are all about national defense aviation and are considered important. It is proposed that the conference decide to recommend that the government adopt and implement them. (Resolution) Passed. (D) Proposal 3, organize the rights to airspace and ban foreigners from flying in the country; Proposal 7, the local governments under the central government shall purchase military aircraft, and the types shall be stipulated by the Ministry of Military Affairs; (Review

Page 9

Continued Important News

Comments) The above two proposals relate to the legal system and are proposed to be submitted to the Second Review Committee for review. (Resolution) Passed.

Regarding auxiliary aviation affairs, a total of 31 proposals: (A) Proposal 1, publicize the aviation industry, prepare to send aircraft to the South Pacific Islands to publicize to overseas Chinese; Proposal 3, propose to send aircraft to comfort overseas Chinese in order to develop the aviation industry; (Review Comments) It is proposed that the conference decide to hand over the above two proposals to the competent authorities for consideration and implementation. (Resolution) Passed. (B) Proposal 2, compile aviation books and unify aviation terms; Proposal 6, standardize aviation terms in order to facilitate education and affairs; Proposal 21, unify aviation terms and vocabulary; (Review Comments) The above three proposals are of the same nature and are considered urgent. It is proposed that the conference decide to use the method of Proposal 6 as the method and hand it over to the competent authorities for adoption and implementation. (Resolution) Passed. (C) Proposal 4, reward ship-air writings to promote and maintain academic research; Proposal 16, reuse specialized talents and reward aviation works; (Review Comments) The above two proposals are of the same nature and are considered acceptable. It is proposed that they be handed over to the competent authorities for consideration and implementation. (Resolution) Passed. (D) Proposal 5, use aviation to conduct actual surveys of the national situation; Proposal 8, conduct aviation surveys to determine the Chinese map; Proposal 12, map the national aviation map (Review Comments) The above three proposals are of the same nature and are considered urgent. The three proposals will be merged and defined as "Conduct aviation surveys to determine the national map." The method will be planned by the General Staff Headquarters in a comprehensive manner, in conjunction with the competent authorities, for separate adoption and gradual implementation. (Resolution) Passed. (E) Proposal 7, expand meteorological observatories; Proposal 14, national aviation meteorological construction; Proposal 15, order the whole country to establish meteorological observatories in urban and rural towns and cities, and add radio stations to important cities; Proposal 17, establish aviation meteorological observatories to facilitate navigation; Proposal 27, request the Aviation Administration to send a letter to the Chinese Meteorological Society, sending letters to domestic meteorological stations and meteorological observatories in various places to provide full assistance to aviation organizations in the area, to liaise and report on meteorological conditions to facilitate flight; Proposal 28, request the establishment of aviation meteorological stations and prepare meteorological observatories at national aviation stations to strengthen aviation safety; Proposal 31, ban foreign meteorological stations in our country and organize national meteorological observatories to strengthen national defense and protect flight and aviation industries; (Review Comments) The above seven proposals are all about meteorological problems, which are extremely important to flight. It is proposed to name them "Establish Aviation Meteorological Observatories." The method is for the aviation authority to separately select from the various proposals and gradually establish them in necessary locations. These observatories will report weather to each other with the existing observatories to facilitate flight. Proposal 31 relates to our country's sovereignty and does not seem to be something that this conference can discuss. It is proposed that the case be sent to the relevant authorities for reference. (Resolution) Passed. (F) Proposal 19, establish an aviation medical research institute to improve aviation medical affairs and improve the effectiveness of aviation personnel; Proposal 22, send personnel abroad to investigate aviation hygiene; Proposal 23, establish a large-scale aviation hospital and establish an aviation physiological hygiene research institute; Proposal 24, increase the number of medical aircraft teams; (Review Comments) The above four proposals relate to medical affairs and should be handed over to the competent authorities for consideration and implementation. (Resolution) Passed. (G) Proposal 10, aviation telegrams should be sent in advance; (Review Comments) This proposal is considered necessary and can be handled by the Aviation Administration and the Ministry of Communications in consultation. (Resolution) Passed. (H) Proposal 13, propose that the Aviation Administration establish a special party branch; (Review Comments) This proposal is considered feasible and it is proposed that the Aviation Administration consult with the Central Party Headquarters to handle it. (Resolution) Reserved. (I) Proposal 25, determine whether the China Aviation Association should continue to exist; (Review Comments) This proposal has a significant impact on the future of aviation and it is proposed that the conference discuss and resolve it. (Resolution) Reserved. (The rest omitted)

Jiang's Bandit Suppression Troops Capture Key Passes in Jiangxi 75

The Right Wing and Middle Route Encircle Donggu

The Left Wing Advances to Shicheng and Ningdu

Luo's Troops Recapture Suichuan in Western Jiangxi

Nanchang correspondence: After the Chiang and Tsai divisions of the 19th Route Army on the right wing recovered Yudu and Xingguo county seats, they occupied the bandit's nest Jiangbei Cave on the Yuxing border. They then defeated the Communist bandits' positions at Ma'anshan, Shazishang, Xikou, and Shihutou, and copied Gulonggang on the Ningdu-Xingguo border, and made contact with Gong's troops occupying Chenggang (on the border of Xingguo, Taihe, Yongfeng, and Ji'an) and Gudu. The Wang Jinyu troops on the middle route, after defeating the bandits at Baisha, Shuinan, and Shuikou (on the border of Jishui, Ji'an, and Yongfeng), and Yaotian and Tengtian (between Yongfeng and Le'an) from Jishui, have advanced to Biaohu, copied the east of Donggu, and heavily surrounded the Communist bandits of Donggu. As for the Zhu Shaoliang troops on the left wing, after capturing Guangchang, they followed and pursued the Communist bandits, and have reached Baishui and Toupi in Guangchang (east of Ningdu), advancing towards Shicheng. The vanguard is no more than a few dozen miles from Shicheng. The Sun Lianzhong troops, after breaking up the famous bandit nest Zhao Xie in Le'an, advanced towards Dongshaokou in Ningdu, supporting the Sixth Route Army in Guangchang and the Fifth Route Army in Yongfeng. Now, apart from a part of the Zhu, Mao, Peng, and Huang bandit gangs who are trapped in Donggu, the Lin Biao, Wu Zhonghao, Chen Yi, and Liu Tiechao bandit gangs have withdrawn from southern Jiangxi and gathered in the corner of Ruijin and Shicheng, intending to flee elsewhere. Therefore, Director He issued a report yesterday saying that the Communist bandits are divided and scattered, with Zhu bandits mainly fleeing to Fujian and Peng bandits mainly fleeing to Hunan, and they will disintegrate. This refers to this situation.

Suichuan in western Jiangxi, bordering Guidong in eastern Hunan, is also a bandit's lair. The former county magistrate, Wang Fan, was brutally killed by bandits. In February, the Li Mingrui gang fled from eastern Hunan to Jiangxi and used this as a base. Although Li's bandits fled into Yongxin later, Suichuan was still occupied by scattered bandits. Director He ordered Luo Lin's troops to advance and suppress them. After receiving the order, Luo advanced along the Gan River towards Taihe and Suichuan, forming a mutual support with the Fourth and Nineteenth Route Armies. According to a telegram from Ji'an on the 17th, the Yi brigade of Luo's troops has cleared the red bandits in Shitoushan, Zaoheshi, Majiazhou, and other places in Taihe, and the Xi brigade has also recovered Suichuan County. The remnants of Li Mingrui's rear have completely fled to Yongxin. The scattered bandits in Wugang, Lantian, and Yutian have also been gradually defeated. The traffic between Taihe, Wan'an, Ganzhou, and Ji'an has been completely restored. After receiving the report, the headquarters ordered the Construction Department to quickly repair the power lines from Ji'an to Ganzhou in order to facilitate traffic and benefit military operations.

Director He said that the disaster situation is extremely serious in the areas occupied by the bandits, so in addition to sending telegrams to all parties to ask for disaster relief, he also telegraphed Xu Shiying, chairman of the Central Relief Committee, yesterday, asking him to personally come to the province to inspect and find ways to provide relief. The Local Consolidation Committee is also currently discussing changing the Finance, Construction, and Education Bureaus of each county into sections, concentrating financial resources for the purpose of operating self-defense groups. Active efforts are also being made to reduce and exempt arrears of land tax in bandit areas and to protect tenant farmers in each county in order to provide post-disaster care.

Headquarters news: Commander-in-Chief Chiang Kai-shek telegraphed the province yesterday, stipulating the rewards and punishments for captured Red bandits, personnel, weapons, and ammunition. Director He has forwarded it to all troops for compliance. The methods are: (1) 300 yuan for capturing a bandit's field gun; (2) 200 yuan for capturing a mortar; (3) 100 yuan for capturing a machine gun; (4) 50 yuan for capturing a pistol; (5) 10 yuan for capturing a rifle. Those who fail to report captured weapons will be severely punished. (April 21)

Recent News on Bandit Suppression on the Guangdong-Jiangxi Border 76

Guangzhou Dispatch: Due to the extensive bandit suppression efforts by various Jiangxi armies near the Guangdong province, there is deep concern that defeated bandits might flee and cause disturbances. Therefore, the Eighth Route Army has specifically ordered the 63rd Division, stationed in the Beijiang area, to move into southern Jiangxi. The 62nd Division, led by Xiang Hanping and stationed in the Dongjiang area, will be deployed to defend the Fujian border. Currently, a regiment of the First Independent Brigade, led by Zhang Ruigui, has already moved into Fengshi and above, and is jointly defending with Zhang Zhen's Fujian army. According to the latest news, the Red Bandits in Jiangxi have been frequently fleeing to eastern Jiangxi, near the border with western Fujian. Moreover, in Liuchexu, Xingning County, Guangdong, a small group of bandits has invaded. The magistrate of Xingning County, fearing the spread of banditry, has urgently telegraphed Commander Xiang in Shantou, requesting him to quickly dispatch five battalions to the county for defense. He has also telegraphed the provincial government to report the situation. Upon receiving the report, the authorities plan to dispatch a unit from Commander Xiang's division to the vicinity to suppress the bandits. As for the Beijiang area, the 19th Route Army continues to station heavy troops in the Xingguo region, as Li Mingrui's forces are currently scattered in eastern Hunan. Strict precautions must be taken to prevent them from linking up with the Red Bandits in eastern Jiangxi. Currently, two brigades of Cai's division have advanced to Longgangxu. Recently, the director of the division's management office, Huang Hechun, and others were specially dispatched back to Guangdong to request military supplies. At the same time, Dai Ji's division has also telegraphed the Guangdong rear affairs office, urging them to quickly recruit and train replacement soldiers to be sent to the front lines. Chen Jitang, considering that Jiang's and Cai's divisions have fought in several provinces and recently suppressed bandits in Jiangxi with great merit, has specially dispatched He Rong, adjutant general of the Eighth Route Army headquarters, to Jiangxi, carrying 100,000 yuan in cash and comfort items such as towels and cigarettes, to reward the officers and soldiers of the two divisions. He Rong, upon receiving the order, departed on the Yuehan train on the 16th to Shaozhou, and will then proceed to Jiangxi. (April 18)

Guangdong Bandits Bomb Three Ships for Several Consecutive Days 77

The Shiqi and Shiqi Ferry Landings Were Repeatedly Bombed by Bandits

A Ferry in Kaiping Sunk After Hitting a Water Mine, Killing Dozens

Guangzhou Dispatch: In Guangdong Province recently, piracy has been rampant and has not subsided. Although naval vessels are said to be patrolling in sections, cases of ship robbery have occurred three times this month. On the evening of the 12th, the Heng'an ferry, which travels between the provincial capital and Shiqi, had a sudden explosion in its passenger cabin shortly after departing from Shiqi. Fortunately, there were not many passengers this time, and no casualties occurred. On the morning of the 13th, at 11:00 AM, the Lianfahe ferry, which travels between Panyu Shiqiao and Shiqi, was about to depart from Shiqi Township when a loud explosion suddenly occurred in the cabin. Fragments of the bomb flew everywhere, immediately injuring three passengers, all of whom were nearby villagers. They were injured in the head, feet, and other areas, and were sent to the municipal hospital for treatment. Both of these ferry bombings were due to prior extortion letters sent by pirates demanding money. The ferry operators ignored them, so they suffered at the hands of the bandits. Only a day or two after these two incidents, the Tongyi Shipping Company in Xihaikou received letters from the Luo Ji Hong bandit gang and the Chen Shiyao bandit gang, demanding 3,000 Hong Kong dollars, several dozen taels of opium, and more than a dozen undershirts, stating that they must be delivered as soon as possible, otherwise, drastic measures would be taken. After receiving the letters, the Tongyi Shipping Company reported to the guild and took strict precautions. Because the bandits' demands were insatiable and impossible to fulfill, and the company had strong capital with eight ferries equipped with guns and cannons for ample self-defense, they did not agree to the bandits' demands that day. The company's largest ferries were the Tongji and Yongfa, which usually travel between Kaiping Taishan and the provincial capital. Security on the ships was extremely tight. The bandits, seeing no way to enter, changed their plans and resorted to external violence, pre-planting water mines in the Shibi waterway in Panyu. The shipowners did not initially notice. On the 17th, when the Tongji and Yongfa ferries were sailing from Kaiping Taishan to the provincial capital, the Tongji ferry went first, followed by the Yongfa ferry. Each ferry carried over a hundred passengers and a large amount of cargo. At 11:20 AM that morning, as they were passing through the Shibi River, where the waterway was narrow, the ships sailed along the center line. Unexpectedly, as it approached just dozens of feet away from the Shibi pier, the Tongji ferry unfortunately struck a water mine, and was immediately bombed. The sound lasted for over a minute. The water sprayed up about ten feet high, and the entire ship shook. The bottom of the Enping (cabin name) cabin was blown open by a large hole, about a foot wide. River water poured in, and the ship began to sink. The cries of the people on board shook the heavens, calling for help. The Xinnanshan tugboat pulling the ferry immediately cut the cable and turned back to rescue. At the same time, the Yongfa ferry, which was sailing behind, also approached to assist. Fortunately, the river was not deep at that location, making rescue easier. As a result, about eighty passengers and crew members from the Tongji ferry were rescued. The remaining forty or fifty people sank into the water with the ship and all drowned. That afternoon, the Xinnanshan and Yongfa ferries transported the rescued people back to the provincial capital. Among them, a crew member named Cen was injured in the explosion and immediately sent to the hospital for treatment. On the 18th, the Fangbian Hospital dispatched over a dozen undertakers with dozens of coffins to the scene of the accident to retrieve the bodies. By the afternoon, over a dozen bodies had been recovered. Many more corpses have not yet surfaced. Afterwards, the Fourth Fleet of the Navy, believing that the Yingjie patrol ship stationed in that section had not provided adequate protection, reprimanded the ship's captain and dispatched the Zhujiang ship to assist in the patrol. (April 19)

Hubei Province Actively Promoting Rural Clearance 78

Rural Clearance Sub-bureaus Have Been Established in All Counties

The General Bureau Has Sent Inspection and Propaganda Officers to Inspect Various Areas

Hankou Dispatch: Since the establishment of the Hubei Rural Clearance General Bureau, Director He Chengjun, Deputy Director Wu Xingya, and Bureau Affairs Director Zhang Gang have been actively proceeding. All rules and regulations have been separately stipulated and orders have been issued to various counties to establish sub-bureaus and implement them accordingly. Currently, all counties in the province have been fully established. In recent days, many have telegraphed the General Bureau to report their establishment, including Wuchang, Hanyang, Huanggang, Qichun, Mianyang, Xiangyang, Jiangling, Hanchuan, Jianli, Zhongxiang, Gucheng, Fangxian, and other twelve counties, each establishing six district sub-bureaus. Huang'an, Echeng, Qishui, Xiaogan, Jingmen, Huangpi, Tianmen, Gong'an, Yingcheng, Suixian, Shishou, Anlu, Jingshan, Zaoyang, Dangyang, Xingshan, Jianshi, Xianfeng, Yicheng, Nanzhang, and Yunxian, Baokang and other twenty-two counties have each established five district sub-bureaus. Luotian, Guangji, Jiayu, Yichang, Puqi, Xianning, Macheng, Chongyang, Yangxin, Daye, Tongshan, Huangmei, Yingshan, Hefeng, Qianjiang, Songzi, Zhijiang, Yidu, Guanghua, Yunmeng, Yunxian, Yuan'an, Badong, Wufeng, Changyang, Enshi, Laifeng, Tongcheng, Zhushan, Yunxi, Zigui, Xuan'en, Lichuan, and Zhuxi, and other thirty-four counties have each established four district sub-bureaus. In total, there is one general bureau and 318 district sub-bureaus in the province. The monthly expenses for each sub-bureau are stipulated at 50 yuan, requiring a monthly total of 15,000 yuan. Together with the General Bureau's expenses of 4,980 yuan, the total is 19,980 yuan. Directors He and Wu, believing that the county bureaus have all been established and that personnel should be sent to supervise and guide the implementation of rural clearance, have specifically divided the province into ten districts and appointed inspection and propaganda officers to inspect each district. The first district is Wuchang, Xianning, Puqi, Jiayu, Tongshan, Chongyang, Tongcheng, Yangxin, and Daye. The second district is Echeng, Huanggang, Qishui, Luotian, Qichun, Huangmei, Guangji, and Macheng. The third district is Huangpi, Xiaogan, Huang'an, Yingshan, Yunmeng, Anlu, Suixian, and Yingcheng. The fourth district is Hanyang, Hanchuan, Mianyang, Qianjiang, Tianmen, Jingshan, and Zhongxiang. The fifth district is Jianli, Shishou, Gong'an, Jiangling, Songzi, Zhijiang, and Yidu, Changyang. The sixth district is Xiangyang, Zaoyang, Yicheng, Nanzhang, Guanghua, and Gucheng. The seventh district is Baokang, Junxian, Fangxian, Yuan'an, Dangyang, and Jingmen. The eighth district is Yunxian, Yunxi, Zhushan, and Zhuxi. The ninth district is Yichang, Zigui, Xingshan, Badong, and Jianshi. The tenth district is Enshi, Xuan'en, Lichuan, Laifeng, Xianfeng, Hefeng, and Wufeng. All are determined according to the railway, Yangtze River, Xiang River, and automobile road transportation situation. As for the inspection and propaganda officers, Lu Shoutu, Wu Bingyuan, Shen Heng, Li Jiugao, Ding Liangyuan, and Liang Shaojun, and other six personnel were announced yesterday and will depart in different directions within days. (April 22)

Suggestions from the Hunan Provincial Party Headquarters 79

Relocate Surrendered Red Bandits from Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi

Request the Government to Issue 100 Million in Public Bonds

To Handle the Relocation Costs to the Northwest

Changsha Dispatch: The Red Bandits in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces are numerous and cause great harm. The central government has separately dispatched troops to conduct a large-scale encirclement and suppression. The period of elimination is expected to be not far off. The primary criminals are unforgivable, but those who blindly follow coercion are not without pity. It seems that they should be allowed to surrender and given a path to self-renewal. However, these people have been intoxicated by the Red Bandits for a long time and are deeply poisoned. Moreover, their previous actions were mostly by hooligans and gangsters who had no permanent property and no legitimate occupations. They should be resettled in a way that they can be reformed. The Hunan Provincial Steering Committee recently received a request from the Changsha City Steering Committee and forwarded it to the central government, requesting the issuance of 100 million yuan in public bonds to cover the cost of relocating surrendered Red Bandits from Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces to the Northwest. This would improve their environment and give them a prosperous life, while also sending personnel to instill the Three Principles of the People in them, so that they can be subtly influenced. The presented document is recorded as follows:

"According to the Changsha City Party Affairs Consolidation Committee's report, the 42nd Committee meeting of the Committee, presented by Committee Member Luo Juju, (Main Text) Request the superiors to forward the central government the case of issuing reclamation public bonds to relocate surrendered Red Bandits from Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces to the Northwest, (Reasons) Investigate the rampant banditry and the chaos everywhere. Now that the army is encircling and suppressing them, the period of annihilation must not be far off. Our central government has a broad mind, using both kindness and authority, allowing those who blindly follow coercion a chance to reform. Reddened masses compete to extricate themselves, so that wherever the flag points, they will collapse at the wind. The amnesty decree is promulgated, and they come back together. This is truly the luck of the party and the country, and the happiness of the people. However, considering that the people, who are good and bad, can they be truly good in nature? Their loss of identity as bandits is due to the seduction of heresy. To be in a difficult situation with one's livelihood, the reason for risking one's life is mostly that of the poor. It is good that our country's economy is backward and its industry is in decline, coupled with frequent natural and man-made disasters, unemployment is increasing day by day, and it is difficult to make a living. The Red Bandits take advantage of this opportunity and falsely advocate the slogan of seeking happiness for the proletariat, or even give small favors to widely seduce the people with naive knowledge and hunger. The poor are easily seduced into banditry and rebellion. For the present plan, on the negative side, efforts should be made to eliminate bandit disasters, and on the positive side, it is especially important to enrich their lives and reform the people's hearts. The ancients said that with enough food and clothing, etiquette and righteousness will flourish. Also, it is said that in prosperous years, children are more reliable, and in bad years, children are more violent. Judging from the present, is that not true? However, the strategy to relieve unemployment is diverse, but immigration and reclamation have the most significant and easy to implement results. The Northwest provinces of our country are vast, the land is fertile, and the climate is mild. All the treasures and forests are undeveloped. Immigrating and reclaiming them is the source of a rich country. The three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi have long been trampled by Red Bandits, and the local vitality is almost exhausted. Even if the entire area is cleared, the aftermath will not be easy. Moreover, the surrendered people have been deeply poisoned and it is difficult to expect them to reform and never take the wrong path again. If they can be relocated to the Northwest, improve their environment, and give them a prosperous life, then boiling water can be prevented by removing the firewood from under the cauldron. It will be easy to do once and for all. Also, the people who are bandits are mostly hooligans and gangsters who have no permanent property and no occupation. Even if they extricate themselves and return, they must set up factories to accommodate them, or lend them money to cultivate the land, so that they can maintain their lives and not be deceived by the Red Bandits. If this fee is used for reclamation, the bandits and the Red Bandits will be cut off forever. Move them to the Northwest, and send personnel from the Party Department to train and instill the Three Principles of the People. They can be subtly influenced. Although the government's expenses are the same, the results are great. Nothing is more important than achieving two goals at once. Therefore, special measures are proposed for selection. Should it be appropriate? Ask the public to decide, (Measures) (1) The central government shall organize the Northwest Reclamation Committee to preside over everything. The number of its members shall be determined by the central government, but at least two shall be assigned from each of the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi. (2) The transfer shall be divided into two phases. The first phase will be strong men, and the second phase will be the old, young, women, and children. However, the first phase must select more workers so that they can build houses first and have a place to live, and then gradually implement reclamation. (3) The reclamation public bond is tentatively set at 100 million yuan. The three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi will be equally divided, with an average of 100,000 Red Bandits in each province, totaling 300,000 people. The average cost per person for agricultural tools, seeds, plowing cattle, and construction is estimated at 100 yuan, totaling 90 million yuan. Schools will be set up for training, hospitals will be opened, and other temporary expenses will be set at 10 million yuan, totaling 100 million yuan. (4) The central government shall issue an order to the National Government's Ministry of Finance to issue the above reclamation public bond in installments. (5) The central government shall issue a notice to the governments of the three provinces of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi, and the military leaders of the bandit suppression, that the surrendered Red Bandits must be sent to the Northwest for reclamation. Each province shall issue passports nearby, and when a certain number of people are gathered, personnel shall be sent to escort them at one time. (6) Those who surrender and are able to live independently in the local area, and who are certified by the local person in charge, are not limited to this. (7) This case shall be decided by this meeting, and submitted to the higher authorities for review and implementation by the central government. It has been discussed by the affiliated association, and it is agreed that relocating the surrendered Red Bandits to the Northwest can solve their lives and develop national treasures. The proposal of Member Luo is an urgent matter. The records are in the file. I hereby submit the case for inspection and instruction. Respectfully submitted, and after being submitted to the 120th Standing Committee of the Association for discussion, it was decided to forward it to the central government for adoption and implementation, and to telegraph the two provinces of Hubei and Jiangxi, requesting them to advocate unanimously. The records are in the file. I hereby submit the case for review and implementation. (Twenty-first)

Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture Revises Cocoon Trading Regulations 81

The Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mines Changed Its Policy of Restricting Cocoon Trading in Order to Encourage

Page 10

The Installation of New-Style Cocoon Drying Machines and the Promotion of Cocoon Drying Cooperatives. The First Meeting of the Provincial Sericulture Design Committee Resolved That Article 4 of the Jiangsu Province Provisional Cocoon Trading Regulations, Which Stipulated That "Counties Where the Amount of Cocoon Drying Exceeds the Amount of Cocoon Production, Any Additional Applications to Establish New Cocoon Trading Businesses, in Addition to Paying 20 Yuan Per Stove, Will Be Subject to an Additional 50 Yuan Surtax," This Measure is Close to Oppressive and Does Not Provide Any Remedy in Fact and Should Be Changed to "Counties Where the Amount of Cocoon Drying Exceeds the Amount of Cocoon Production, No Cocoon Trading Business Without New-Style Cocoon Drying Machine Equipment May Apply to Establish a Business," Also, Because Article 8 of the Original Regulations Stipulated That Farmers' Cocoon Drying Technology Was Immature and Easily Damaged the Quality of the Cocoons, It Was Resolved to Abolish the Farmers' Own Cocoon Stoves and Actively Promote Cocoon Drying Cooperatives. In addition, Article 10 of the Original Regulations on the Scope of Penalties Did Not Stipulate Anything for Cocoon Trading Businesses Holding Cocoon Licenses Arbitrarily Relocating Their Addresses or Transferring Ownership, Which Often Caused Disputes and Made Supervision Inconvenient. It is Also Appropriate to Take Measures to Ban It. The Bureau Has Separately Revised Them and Submitted Them to the Provincial Government Committee Meeting on the 10th of This Month for Approval and Ordered All Counties to Comply. The Revised Regulations Are Recorded Below:

Jiangsu Province Provisional Cocoon Trading Regulations (Article 1) All Counties in Jiangsu Province May Establish Cocoon Trading Businesses. (Article 2) Any Citizen of the Republic of China May Submit an Application to the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mines for Review and Then Transfer It to the Education Funding Management Office of the Department of Finance to Issue a Business License to Establish a Cocoon Trading Business Within the Province. The Application Must State: 1. The Name of the Applicant, 2. The Occupation and Address of the Applicant, 3. The Name of the Cocoon Trading Business, 4. The Nature of the Organization, 5. The Location of the Cocoon Trading Business, 6. The Number of Cocoon Stoves and the Amount of Cocoon Drying, 7. The Name, Type, and Style of the Cocoon Stoves, 8. The Number of Dry Cocoon Loads Produced in the County in the Year With the Most Cocoon Production, 9. The Number of Cocoon Trading Businesses Already Established in the County and the Number of Cocoon Stoves. (Article 3) After Submitting the Application, the Department of Agriculture and Mines Will Review It in Accordance With the Following Two Paragraphs: 1. Whether the Amount of Cocoon Drying by the Cocoon Stoves Already Established in the County Exceeds the Amount of Cocoon Production by More Than 20%, 2. The Applicant's Citizenship Qualifications. (Article 4) In Counties Where the Amount of Cocoon Drying Exceeds the Amount of Cocoon Production in Paragraph 1 of the Previous Article, No Cocoon Trading Business Without New-Style Cocoon Drying Machine Equipment May Apply to Establish a Business. If It Is Found That the Applicant Has Lost Their Citizenship Qualifications in Paragraph 2, the Issuance of a Cocoon License May Be Suspended. (Article 5) Any Application That Has Been Reviewed by the Department of Agriculture and Mines and Is in Accordance With the Two Items Mentioned Above May Be Sent to the Education Funding Management Office of the Department of Finance for Approval and the Issuance of a Cocoon License to Begin Business. (Article 6) The Cocoon License Fee is 20 Yuan Per Stove. Anyone With an Old License Will Pay Half Price to Cancel It. The Handling Fee is Uniformly 1 Yuan Per Stove. The Effective Period of a New License is Limited to Ten Years. The Business Tax is 1 Yuan Per Year. (Article 7) The License Fee for a New-Style Cocoon Drying Machine is Based on the Number of Stoves and the Amount of Cocoon Drying. (Article 8) Any Cocoon Drying Cooperative Organized by Farmers That Has Been Certified by the County Bureau of Construction and the Cooperative Business Instructor as Being Used by the Farmers Themselves for Cocoon Drying and Not Leased to Cocoon Merchants or Silk Merchants, the Cocoon License Fee May Be Reduced to 5 Yuan Per Stove. (Article 9) A Cocoon Trading Business That Has Received a Business License May Dry Cocoons on Behalf of Farmers, but the Fee Must Be Handled in Accordance With the Prices Stipulated by the County Bureau of Construction or the County Government and May Not Be Changed Without Authorization. (Article 10) Any Cocoon Trading Business That Has Not Obtained a Cocoon License or a Local Stove Privately Established by Farmers Will Be Confiscated and Subject to a Fine of Between 100 and 400 Yuan Upon Discovery. After Obtaining a Cocoon License, Any Relocation of the Business Address or Transfer of Ownership That Has Not Been Reported for Record Will Have Its Cocoon License Revoked. (Article 11) These Regulations Will Be Implemented From the Date of Promulgation.

Thriving Strategies for the Jiangsu Provincial Capital's Business District 82

Proposals to Dredge Duck Pond River and the East and West Intercalary Rivers

Remedies Are Possible for the Old Marketplace Before the New Marketplace is Complete

Section 2 of Zhongzheng Road Decided to Use Route A

Zhenjiang Dispatch: The Jiangsu Construction Department convened a meeting of the Provincial Capital Construction Advisory Council at 2:00 PM yesterday. Attendees included Hou Zhenping, Lin Wenqin, Su Zengyi, Qiu Yu, Zhang Jianming, Lu Xiaobo, Bao Mingshu, Hu Jianchun, Leng Yuqiu, Zhang Yisun, Yu Xiaochuan, Chen Fu, and Ye Jiajun. Ye Jiajun chaired the meeting. This was the first Advisory Council meeting since the reorganization of the Construction Committee. The Engineering Department proposed the route problem for Section 2 of Zhongzheng Road, dividing it into two routes, A and B. It was decided to use Route A. The reason being that there is no need for a road to be perfectly straight. The houses demolished by Route B would all be demolished through the center of people's houses, causing great losses to the people. According to the proposal's description, Route A has more advantages than Route B. Later, Advisors Leng, Lu, Hu, Yu, Bao, Zhang, Hou, and Lin successively stated their opinions on the question of how to remedy the shallowing of the Jiangtan in the old business district of the provincial capital. They also invited Mao Yisheng, Director of the Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau, to attend the discussion, believing that it was necessary to dredge the Intercalary River. It is noted that the Provincial Government has resolved to open Xiangshan Port as a new marketplace on a grand scale, which is welcomed by public opinion in the provincial capital. However, the reason why the Provincial Government abandoned the old marketplace is that the Jiangtan rises day by day and will become wasteland. Therefore, it abandons the old and seeks the new, using it as a fundamental solution. However, the rise of the Jiangtan is due to the changing river flow, with the northern torrent being faster than the southern gradual flow. If the river flow is not changed, and only the marketplace is moved eastward, there is a risk that Xiangshan Port will also be shallow in the long run. (On the south bank of Jiaoshan, the water flow was originally more rapid than on the north side of Jiaoshan and unfathomable, but in recent years the north side of Jiaoshan has become more rapid than the south side of the river, and shoals have been found at the foot of Xiangshan). This is one of the reasons. Xiangshan Port is an open space, and the roads and various buildings will naturally cost less, but it is impossible for the industries and businesses of Zhenjiang, which were originally in the western district, to completely move to the new marketplace. As a result, the old marketplace may not be able to revive, and the new marketplace may not be able to complete, and the prosperity of the provincial capital will remain only an ideal. This is the second reason. The cost of operating the new marketplace, according to the budget for the use of construction public bonds, is more than 1.63 million yuan, but the Provincial Government previously had a resolution to open a pilot high-area construction zone in the city. The drawing plan and land registration have been underway for some time, and the cost is only a part of the 700,000 yuan in construction funds for the provincial capital, but it has been suspended to this day due to lack of funds. Then, the 1.6 million yuan plan for the new port is even more difficult to implement. If we do not start by maintaining the old marketplace first, the establishment of the new marketplace will be a distant prospect. The old one has been abandoned, and the new one has not been completed. Zhenjiang's industry and commerce will be retired. This is the third reason. It is noted that the construction public bonds list 300,000 yuan for the reorganization of port affairs, which is not a small amount, but compared with 1.6 million yuan, it is not much. Dredging the Intercalary River is a stopgap measure, and opening Xiangshan Port is a fundamental cure. Before Xiangshan Port is completed, the Intercalary River must be dredged first to maintain the old marketplace, so as to wait for the completion of the new marketplace. There will be no shortage in between. This is the fourth reason. Director Mao Yisheng also explained the reasons for opening the new port: (1) Xiangshan Port can be guaranteed not to be shallow for 60 years, (2) It is difficult to guarantee that the Intercalary River will not be shallow again in the future, (3) Changing the river flow is a huge project. Not only is there construction in Guazhoutou in Jiangbei, but also major projects in Runzhou, which costs too much, and so on. After a long discussion, the meeting suggested that the Construction Department provide the Provincial Government with reference, and the proposal was titled "Proposal to Dredge Duck Pond River and the East and West Intercalary Rivers to Prosper the Provincial Capital's Commerce." The meeting adjourned at about 4:00 PM.

Russian Province of Amu Darya Expels Chinese Farmers 83

Implementing Policy to Suppress Small Farmers

A dispatch from Jilin states that the Amu Darya province is the granary of the Russian Far East, particularly the area along the Jingqi and Heilongjiang (Amur) river basins, known for its fertile lands. On the left bank of the river is the Tangbo Fu Ke district, its southeast side being the Sixty-Four Villages East of the River seized by Russia. During the Boxer Rebellion, hundreds of our farmers were driven into the turbulent river by the Russian governor-general Gribsky, perishing at the hands of foreigners in this very land. For thirty years, our countrymen have seemingly forgotten this tragedy, and those who have tilled this land with their plows have once again gathered like ants. Moreover, after the establishment of the Soviet government, all land was nationalized, and to prevent it from lying barren, they loudly proclaimed slogans such as abolishing national boundaries and the sanctity of labor and agriculture, vigorously attracting settlers. The Russian government even allocated seeds and banks provided capital assistance. Of the agricultural harvest, the state takes six parts, and the tenants receive four. As a result, even more families came. Recently, the government, seeing that the communist policies are gradually taking effect, and that the wealthy and large farmer classes have been completely crushed, no longer fearing their rebellion, has now taken a further step to suppress small farmers. Those private farmers in that country who have not joined agricultural cooperatives are often having their assets confiscated, forced to gather firewood in the mountains or driven to the remote frontiers to develop the borderlands. Taking the Tangbo Fu Ke district as an example, nearly all farmers in that country who have not joined agricultural cooperatives have now been expelled. There are about forty Chinese tenant households scattered in this area who have not acquired Russian citizenship, but because they are still under the protection of the consulate, they cannot be arbitrarily handled like the citizens of that country. Therefore, the authorities have first declared that all their land will be reclaimed, and their cattle and horses will be impounded, awaiting further orders. The intention is to force them to join the cooperatives. If they join as members, they must hand over all their cattle, horses, and farm implements to be used as shares in the cooperative. The annual interest and surplus are recorded in a small booklet, nominally distributed as extra profits, but in reality, they cannot be freely used. As for daily necessities, the restrictions are even stricter. Apart from a fixed amount of flour, salt, and other items, almost nothing else can be obtained. Therefore, these overseas Chinese farmers are currently in a very difficult situation. Joining the cooperative would mean sinking even deeper, but not joining means they cannot survive. They are truly trapped in a helpless situation. In short, wherever Soviet law reaches, whether for its own citizens or foreigners, it aims to ensure that, beyond barely providing enough to eat and wear, no one possesses significant property. If they do, it will be confiscated according to law. If the law is insufficient, new clauses will be created to supplement it. This is the case for private merchants, and it is the same for farmers and workers. As for the protective power of the consulate, it only extends to the scope of the law. For example, the land rented in the Tangbo Fu Ke district has no fixed term, nor is there a contract. The government reserves the right to reclaim it at any time. The consulate can only request that the movable property of these tenant farmers be allowed to be freely sold and returned to their home country, but even this is very difficult.

Local Dispatches

Songjiang 84

Transfer of Prison Warden. Prison Warden Zhang Zonglie has been transferred to the position of Prison Warden and Head of the Detention Center in Jiangyin County by order of the High Court. Xu Qi will succeed Zhang. The handover was completed today (the 23rd). It is said that Mr. Zhang will rest for a while before going to Cheng to take up his new post.

Female Corpse Found in Xiuye Bridge River. Today, the body of a woman was found in the Xiuye Bridge River. The local bailiff reported it to the court prosecutor, who went to examine it in the afternoon. The body has been identified by family member Zhang Jinqi as his daughter, who had been missing for several days. She was seventeen years old and had been betrothed to someone. The matter arose because Wu Jingqing, the owner of a cigarette shop in the Hualou section of the Yue Temple, had two hundred small coins stolen on the 17th. Since his niece (Zhang's daughter) had come to the shop that day, she was suspected. He asked someone to invite her back for questioning. The girl even undressed to show her innocence. Her father, upon learning of this, scolded her. She went missing the next day. Zhang Jinqi went to Wu Jingqing to demand that she be found. They argued, and the Public Security Bureau was informed, who fined Zhang three yuan for damaging items in the shop. He was extremely angry and filed a lawsuit with the County Court for investigation. Unexpectedly, his daughter had already committed suicide by drowning herself. It is unknown how this tragic case will be resolved.

Wuxi 85

Robbery and Assault in Xin'an Township. Du Zhoumin, a resident of Xidu Jia in the Thirteenth District (Xin'an Township), is a wealthy widow with hundreds of acres of fertile land. Her husband, Du Zanping, has passed away. At about 8 PM on the 22nd, more than ten bandits suddenly arrived, speaking with local accents, and armed with handguns, iron rulers, and flashlights. They broke down the door and tied up Du Zhoumin, forcing her to reveal the location of her hidden silver. When Du Zhoumin was slow to respond, the bandits beat her with clubs, causing several serious injuries. The bandits then went through the house, searching and looting extensively. They stole 250 yuan in cash. The homes of Du Ronglin and Du Ting'an, who lived together, were also robbed of gold, silver jewelry, clothing, and other items, worth approximately 100 yuan.

Tenth Sub-Bureau Arrests Large Number of Gamblers. Huang Ren, the chief of the Tenth Sub-Bureau of the County's Ninth District, Houqiao Township Public Security Bureau, received a report the day before yesterday (the 22nd) that gambling and illegal opium sales were taking place near Shengjia Bridge. Chief Huang immediately dispatched a senior police officer, who found a large number of gamblers rolling dice and smoking opium. Sixteen people, including Pu Zuyin, Zhou Junbao, and Sheng Hengshang, were arrested and detained overnight. The next morning, they were escorted to the city and transferred to the County Court for questioning.

Verdict in Qitai Inn Bloodshed Case. Xiang Afu and Gu A'er, temporary cooks at the Qitai Inn on the road, had an argument over fifteen copper coins on the 19th of last month. In a fit of rage, A'er used an iron shovel to kill Xiang Afu. Afterwards, Gu A'er surrendered to the County Court, which interrogated and detained him. The prosecutor's office filed a public prosecution. It is now learned that yesterday was the day for the verdict. Judge Liang opened the court and brought Gu A'er from the detention center. The main text of the verdict was announced: Gu A'er was sentenced to nine years of imprisonment and ten years of deprivation of civil rights.

Three Robberies Occur Near the City. A shrimp cage boat moored under the Chendu Bridge outside the South Gate of Wuyi was robbed on the morning of the 22nd. All silver coins and clothing were taken away. The bandits then went to the Ye family's home in Xiatang to rob. After breaking into the house, they locked the family members in one room and then looted at will, causing heavy losses. At about 8 PM that night, a incense boat returning from Maoshan under the Xiaocang Bridge was suddenly boarded by eight bandits armed with handguns. All the cash and valuables hidden on the bodies of the pilgrims were looted.

Joint Military and Police Operation to Suppress Bandits. Zhu Mian, commander of the Su-Chang Pacification Division, deeply resents the repeated kidnapping and robbery cases in the eastern townships. A plan was made on the 20th to secretly order the military and police to conduct a search and suppression operation in three routes: east, central, and north. Zhenjiang 88

Pacification Command Executes Bandits. Yu, the battalion commander of the Fourth Battalion of the Third Security Regiment of Jiangsu Province, previously captured Ma Xiande, the platoon leader of the defense corps who secretly colluded with bandit leaders to share the spoils, and Jiang Hengmin, who conspired with kidnappers to demand ransom, in the Niuyutao area. After interrogation at the Ningzhen District Pacification Command, they confessed to the charges. They were sentenced to death in accordance with the regulations for punishing bandits. The execution was approved by Pacification Commissioner Zhang. Therefore, yesterday, the two criminals were tied up in the Niuyutao area and executed by firing squad. Also, the Pacification Command previously captured Gong Zhaolin, a bandit quartermaster, because he secretly contacted bandits Chen Wenqi, Bao Si, and Wang Jingui under the guise of running a store to negotiate the ransom of kidnapped victims and hand over money. After investigation, the facts were verified and he confessed to the charges. After being approved by the Pacification Commissioner's Office for execution, the bandit was also identified yesterday and escorted to the vicinity of Qiaotou Town for execution by firing squad.

Yangzhou 89

Complex Incest Case. The incest case involving a brother and sister, who are suspected of helping the brother kill his sister-in-law, which has shocked the city, has drawn great attention from the public and the Public Security Bureau. After the First Sub-Bureau of the Public Security Bureau reported the details of the case to the General Bureau, the judicial section twice summoned Jiang Youmei, the deceased's husband, but he did not appear. He was then ordered to be brought in on bail. He was apprehended by the guarantor and the police at the Xiannv Temple and brought to the bureau. Tang, the head of the judicial section, conducted a preliminary interrogation, during which Jiang said that his wife had indeed died of illness. Because the neighbors often borrowed money from him without success, they fabricated this shocking rumor after his wife's death. He also said that the person living with him was his sister-in-law, not his biological sister. Since the case involved judicial matters, Chief Tang attached the original documents and sent them to the court's prosecutor's office for detailed investigation. However, it is said that the case involves many suspected impostors and extortionists, and has attracted the attention of Pacification Commissioner Zhang, who has arrested a person named Ge and handed him over to the military law office for detailed interrogation. The matter is expanding and may not be resolved in the short term.

Nantong 91

Fishermen in Tong, Rugao, Hai'an, and Qidong Resume Operations. Fishermen in Tongzhou, Rugao, Hai'an, and Qidong counties along the coast north of the Yangtze River had previously suspended operations due to rampant pirate activity in the sea. Now that the fishing protection and bandit suppression teams have cleared the pirates, fishermen resumed operations on the 21st, coinciding with the Guyu (Grain Rain) fishing season. Over 500 fishing boats left port. The Coastal Defense Command has dispatched warships such as the Hai Ou to provide protection at sea.

Finance Bureau Busy Collecting Back Taxes and Grain. The amount of back taxes and grain owed in Tongzhou is substantial. The Finance Bureau has dispatched officials to collect it. Households with excessive arrears are being detained by the County Government until the debt is paid.

Jiaxing 92

Detailed Report on the Robbery in Shiwan. Shiwan Town, located at the junction of Chongde and Tongxiang in Jiaxing, is a prosperous market town with densely packed residences. It was previously looted by retreating soldiers in 1927. Afterwards, business gradually recovered. Unexpectedly, several bandit boats arrived the day before yesterday and looted the town again. The town's water police team lost seventeen guns, and the Tongxiang and Chongde Public Security Bureaus lost eight rifles. The militia also had firearms stolen. Almost no shops or residences were spared. The Gongtai and Jitong pawnshops each suffered losses of more than 10,000 yuan. The total loss for the entire town is estimated at approximately 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. Twelve people, including police officers, patrols, and Jitong pawnshop employees Xie Wenxi and Chen Guosheng, were injured. The county magistrates of Tongxiang and Chongde, the chiefs of the Public Security Bureaus, and Party members have visited the town to investigate and discuss relief measures.

Hangzhou 94

Xin Yuan Gold Shop Robbed. The largest gold shops in Hangzhou are Xin Yuan, Qian Yuan, and Yi Yuan on Jianqiao Road. Each has a tall, five-story Western-style building. Xin Yuan is the oldest and most reputable, so its business is very prosperous. Yesterday (the 23rd) at about 2 PM, six bandits suddenly arrived, all wearing blue-gray serge robes and bronze basin hats, appearing well-dressed. The shop thought they were customers. Unexpectedly, two of the six men guarded the door, two jumped over the counter, drove the employees to a corner, and the other two searched for gold jewelry. After about five minutes, they walked out in single file, escaping towards Jewelry Lane. It is said that the stolen jewelry is worth more than 20,000 yuan.

Now, the Public Security Bureau is planning to double the tax. The rickshaw operators oppose this, saying they cannot afford it. Negotiations are currently underway.

Notorious Bandit Killed, Kidnapped Victims Rescued. Yesterday, the second township clearing sub-bureau searched Xinzhuang and saw the notorious bandit Chen Junting and others carrying guns. The police immediately tried to arrest them, but the bandits resisted by opening fire. The police returned fire, killing the notorious bandit Chen Junting and capturing Wang Yulan. Wang Yulan and Liang San were presented to the County Clearing Bureau today for questioning.

Letters to the Editor

Letter from Douglas Paul 99

Having recently read the news item “U.S. Church Fundraising Scandal” in the Overseas News section of your paper on April 20, I must state that the details mentioned do not conform to the facts and may easily cause readers to misunderstand. The missionary work of Christianity in various countries is extensive, and the work is also diverse. Constant improvement is, of course, a necessary plan. Therefore, a group of enthusiastic church members in the United States who are dedicated to overseas missionary work elected representatives to come to various Eastern countries (such as China, Japan, India, etc.) to re-examine the overseas missionary work. Our delegation has now arrived in China and is diligently engaged in investigations. We will report to our country this year. Afterwards, other American church groups will come to China based on our investigation report to assess the value of the work to promote improvements. The purpose is to promote the development of the church and the efficiency of the work. There is no “arbitrary and wasteful spending of donations and failure to use them for proper purposes” as reported in yesterday's newspaper. I fear that misinformation will spread and cause misunderstandings. Therefore, I am writing to request a correction. Respectfully, Douglas Paul, Chairman of the U.S. Church Overseas Missionary Work Investigation Delegation, April 23.

Education News

Important News

Ministry of Education 100

Commendation for Guangdong Education Department's Reorganization of Private Schools

The Ministry of Education, upon receiving a report from the Guangdong Education Department on the progress of banning unregistered and poorly run private middle schools, instructed the department: "Having received your report, the people of your province should respond to the needs of the times and actively establish middle schools to supplement the inadequacies of public schools, which is a good phenomenon in education. The department's ability to distinguish between good and bad and actively provide guidance is commendable. However, the educational goals and implementation guidelines of the Republic of China clearly state that ordinary education must cultivate national morality and foster life skills and enhance productive capacity. The instructions are very detailed. In the future, if people in your province are interested in establishing middle schools, they should be instructed to focus on vocational education. Then, elementary school graduates will not only be spared the plight of having nowhere to study but will also be able to support themselves and serve society after leaving school. This is much more beneficial than focusing solely on ordinary middle schools. The department should pay attention to this when reviewing applications from private individuals to establish middle schools."

National Jinan University and Central University 101

Songjiang Education Investigation Team Returns to Shanghai

The Songjiang Education Investigation Team, jointly organized by National Jinan University and Central University, has completed its work in Songjiang after one week (from the 13th to the 20th of this month). The investigation items are divided into society, educational administration, school buildings, funding, physical examinations, student status, teacher evaluation, teaching methods, curriculum, intelligence, and academic testing. A total of 20 schools in the urban and rural areas, 3,800 students, and more than 200 teachers and staff were investigated. During the work, the head of the Education Bureau, Ni Han Chen, the inspector Zhang, the section chief Zhu, and the principals and teachers of various schools all provided enthusiastic assistance. All the instructors and investigators also worked very hard, so it was possible to complete the investigation in a short time. During the investigation period, Bureau Chief Ni, Songjiang Middle School, Songjiang Women's Middle School, and the alumni associations of Central University and Southeast University hosted banquets. The Education Bureau also convened a discussion meeting with all the principals and teachers in the city and invited the instructors to speak. In recent days, various schools have invited instructors Xie Xunchu, Cheng Zhichiu, Tai Shuangqiu, and Xia Zhanchu to give lectures. The team members held an entertainment gala the night before last. The results of this work include four large boxes of testing forms and 30 to 40 temporary photos. All the data will be organized before the summer vacation. Yesterday, the team members from the two schools returned to Shanghai. The team members from Central University immediately transferred to Nanjing.

Director Xu of the Municipal Education Bureau 114

Speaks to the Liangjiang Women's Basketball Team

The Liangjiang Women's Sports School basketball team is scheduled to depart for Japan tomorrow. Principal Lu of the school believes that this trip concerns the national image and carries significant responsibility. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, he specially invited Xu Peihuang, Director of the Municipal Education Bureau, to the school to address the entire team. The main points of Director Xu's speech were that Japanese women's sports are highly developed, and before departing, they should practice diligently. He noted that Japanese women are tall, so they should not be intimidated and should bravely move forward to achieve victory in everything. He also stressed the importance of paying attention to the virtues of cleanliness, orderliness, diligence, and simplicity in Japan. He concluded by saying that winning or losing is not the main concern. Principal Lu expressed his gratitude and led Director Xu on a tour of the various departments of the school, which Xu seemed pleased with. It was also learned that Mr. Ota of the Shanghai branch of the Asahi Shimbun assisted in arranging the ship tickets and cabins, and Ota also telegraphed various Japanese organizations and news agencies to request publicity and hospitality. Later, Principal Lu and Ota had a three-point conversation, stating that the purpose of the trip was to observe the state of women's sports in Japan, promote friendship between Chinese and Japanese women in sports, and improve the players' basketball skills.

The Chinese Tennis Club Will Open 115

From May to September

The Chinese Tennis Club on Route Frelupt has completed the repair of its courts and will begin playing tennis to meet the seasonal demand. There are four types of membership available, and registration can be done at the Shanghai Amateur Athletic Federation starting today. The regulations are listed below:

Regulations of the Shanghai Chinese Tennis Club

1. This club is organized by the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation and is named the Shanghai Chinese Tennis Club.

2. The tennis season will run from May to the end of September. 3. Membership is divided into four categories: Ordinary, Affiliate (Student), Women's, and Special (Foreign).

4. Entrance fees are: Ordinary members, 15 yuan; Affiliate members, 12 yuan; Women members, 10 yuan; Special members, 20 yuan.

5. The club provides workers, nets, and ball boys. Only members who have paid the entrance fee are allowed to play on the courts.

6. Playing hours are from 4:00 PM daily. On Saturdays, Sundays, and Sunday mornings from 9:00 AM, practice is also allowed.

7. The club has a committee to manage club affairs. A secretary will be concurrently appointed by the Amateur Athletic Federation.

8. Members bringing friends to play tennis must wait until the courts are free before joining in, and must sign the register each time and pay a small fee of four dimes. If a non-member plays at the club more than three times, the club may request them to pay the fee and become a member to show restraint and avoid hindering the rights of members.

9. To join the club, one must register and pay the fee at the Chinese National Amateur Athletic Federation on Route Frelupt, and provide contact information and phone number for easy communication.

10. After joining, the club will issue a membership badge, which must be worn when playing on the courts for identification.

11. The club may temporarily suspend playing during rainy weather or when the ground is wet, or when formal competitions are held.

12. Members should abide by the rules and give way to club affairs during formal competitions, refraining from practice.

13. If there are many members playing tennis, they should take turns entering the court, and play doubles as a principle, limited to one hour to ensure equal opportunity and benefits for all members.

14. Shoes with heels or hard leather soles are not allowed on the courts to avoid damaging the playing surface.

15. When playing tennis, attire should be neat and tidy. Vests and long gowns should not be worn to maintain appearances.

16. Members should absolutely comply with the advice of the committee and club staff.

17. These regulations are subject to amendment at any time as necessary.
