Page 11

Free Talk

Global Tidbits 118

—Hai Ke

Fashionable women in England and America generally possess two types of wedding rings. One is a plain gold or platinum band, devoid of any embellishments, used exclusively for daytime wear. In the evening, they wear a different wedding ring, one that is encrusted with diamonds all around.

Europe experienced an unprecedented rainy season in November of 1929. Most areas were inundated with rain. In England and Wales alone, the rainfall amounted to two trillion tons.

A philanthropist in London specializes in collecting discarded garbage and waste, employing scientific methods to transform the useless into something useful, thereby generating income. He established an orphanage that houses one thousand orphans. For the past twenty years, the annual expenses have been entirely covered by the proceeds from these garbage and waste materials.

A new public library was established in Hendon, England, at the cost of forty thousand pounds. It includes a dedicated children's room stocked with children's books and periodicals for them to read. It also has a children's restroom where they can wash their hands before reading to avoid soiling the books.

Female employees in British public institutions who resign upon marriage, after serving for six years, receive six months' salary as a marriage stipend.

Detailed Record of the Election of National Assembly Representatives from the Chamber of Commerce 119

—Sun Choucheng

The election of representatives to the National Assembly has concluded in Shanghai. From the business sector, Wang Yansong, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, was elected. The general situation has been reported in various newspapers. This undertaking was highly valued by the late Premier, and was solemnly stated in his will. Therefore, Choucheng also went to participate on that day. This record of what was seen, it is assumed, will also be welcomed by those who care about national affairs.

On that day, the national flag was hung high above the entrance of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. Patrol officers dispatched by the Public Security Bureau, along with the chamber's security team, stood fully armed on both sides. The hall was in the assembly hall on the second floor. A registration desk was set up at the entrance, staffed by Zheng Chengqing, Sun Mingqi, Jin Shengbai, and Xue Guangqian as managers. After the representatives of various industries signed their names and the names of their respective guilds, they were given a strip of white cloth, serving as the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce National Assembly Representative Election Number X Entry Permit. Only then could they enter the venue to vote. Three rows of representative seats were set up inside the venue, each row with three lines, and each line with nine seats. Pens, ink, and water dishes were provided for filling out the ballots. Wang Xiaolai, wearing a red satin badge of the "Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Election Supervisor," sat to the left of the ballot box. It is said that he arrived at the meeting at 7:30 AM. It was stipulated today that the ballots would be counted at 4:00 PM, requiring him to work for ten hours straight, unable to leave his post. Even meals had to be brought to the ballot box. Since leaving his study, he had never sat so still. Out of necessity, he brought various tabloids and the Thirteen Classics Compilation published by the Commercial Press to pass the time. He also said that the chamber of commerce electoral roll had a total of three hundred and ninety-three voters. The license plate number of his car was also three hundred and ninety-three. What a coincidence! However, he had declared that he would exercise his right to vote in Sheng County. Therefore, although he was an election supervisor in today's election, he had neither the right to vote nor the right to be elected. Voting manager Ding Shoutang wore a yellow badge, and ballot counting manager Shao Baosan wore a blue badge. They both sat on the right side of the stage. When representatives from various industries came to collect ballots, Mr. Ding checked their names against the electoral roll and asked them to sign the voting register in person before handing over the ballot. The ballot paper was white with blue lettering, about four inches long and two inches wide, resembling a Western-style envelope. Inside was a rectangular shape marked with a thin line. Above was the phrase "Nominee," with a space in the middle and the word "Name" beside it, to be filled with the nominee's name. Below was the word "Voter," and the voter was required to fill in their own name. Otherwise, the ballot would be considered invalid. The ballot and the sealing flap were stamped with the seals of the election supervisor, both large and small. Supervisor Mayor Zhang wanted to inspect various universities and freelance groups also holding elections at the same time. Therefore, he arrived at the meeting at 8:30 AM, took a brief look, sat for a short time, and then left. On that day, cars and chartered vehicles came and went like shuttles within the Chamber of Commerce. Zheng Chengqing was the first representative to sign in, earning the number one spot. Pei Yunqing and Fang Jiaobo signed in at the same time, one as number sixty-three and the other as number sixty-four. Pei jokingly said to Fang, "You and I can be considered brothers." Wang Yansong received a total of one hundred and seventy votes. However, one of the ballots had added a wood radical to the "Yan" character in his name, rendering it invalid. Therefore, the newspapers announced that he had won with one hundred and sixty-nine votes.

Romanian Crown Prince Visits China 120

— Xin Fo

Romanian Crown Prince Bibesco is the president of the International Air League and is renowned in the aviation community. He recently embarked on a tour of East Asia and set out from Paris at the end of March, passing through Saigon, Vietnam, and other places before flying to Shanghai. He will then return west, inspecting famous airfield stations along the way. He will also conduct a thorough inspection of China's aviation industry. The aircraft he is traveling in is the Ford Motor Company-produced A.T. No. 5 Pullman-style all-steel three-engine large aircraft, the same type that recently carried the Prince of Wales and Prince George on their tour of South America.

Record of a Visit to the Jiangwan Branch of Xiaoguan Garden 121

— Qionghan

I have visited the main garden of Xiaoguan Garden many times. However, the Jiangwan branch is slightly remote. Since its opening in the autumn, I had only stopped there once during the chrysanthemum exhibition. Nearly half a year has passed without me having the time to set foot there again. A few days ago, the garden owner, Mr. Yang Shouchun, informed me that the peach and plum blossoms in the garden were in full bloom, and the cyclamens were vying for beauty, making it worth a visit. He specially arranged a banquet in the garden on Sunday and invited Wu Zilianzhou, Shao Yiqun, Tian Jihen, and myself for a day's excursion. Previously, Mr. Qian Junchuan had suggested gathering for breakfast at Wufangzhai, setting a time limit from 7:00 AM to 8:00 AM. I found the conditions too strict and discussed with Yiqun not participating, choosing to go our separate way. We did not reach our destination until near noon. Although the weather was not sunny that day, fortunately the overnight rain had cleared, which was enough to inspire us. The scenery along the way was particularly charming. As we approached the garden gate, we caught sight of an eagle soaring in the sky, as if touching the clouds. Yiqun and I were deeply amazed. Upon entering the garden, we learned that it was the painter Mr. Zhang Guangyu who was playing the trick of the wind calligrapher there. After a short delay, Lianzhou came out from inside, and upon seeing us, exclaimed with joy, "The eaters have arrived!" After a short pause, I toured the flowerbeds. I indeed saw the radiant and blooming cyclamens, as splendid as brocade. The flowerbeds were all newly planted with famous chrysanthemum seedlings. In one place, it was like curtains hanging low, with dwellings visible from afar. Each cluster was planted with peonies taller than my shoulder, laden with buds. Although there were already some that had broken their calyxes, the flowers were only half-open. Although it is said that the spring is still cold and the flower season is somewhat delayed, these beautiful and famous flowers, resembling a seventeen or eighteen-year-old bride, were entirely veiled in light chiffon, creating an enchanting posture that far surpasses those who lightly reveal their beauty. I heard from Shouchun that these two clusters of peonies have been around for decades, and are not easily found today. They were originally in the garden of a certain wealthy family. Due to the reconstruction of their house, there was no space to accommodate them. The cost of these two branches was almost the entire property of an average person. If one wanted to find something similar, it would not be easy to obtain even at twice the price. During the banquet that day, Mr. Tian Jihen's enthusiasm for wine was particularly strong. He even raised his glass repeatedly with Mr. Wang Yongkang and Mr. Qian Junchuan, who were sitting across the table, causing surprise. Some said that Mr. Tian had newly taken a concubine and was deliberately in high spirits, unapproachable. It seems that he plans to hold a banquet in the garden next Sunday, not only because he loves the location being isolated from the hustle and bustle, but also because he has thoroughly read the line "hiding the beauty from his wife" in the Story of the Western Wing. That evening, I stayed late due to playing mahjong in the garden. Mr. Yang kindly offered to drive me home. Before leaving, he also gifted me with many pots of exotic flowers. Thus, I returned with blooming flowers. Therefore, this journey is particularly worthy of recording.

More Than Ten Days Since the Ye Chen Case Trial Began 122

— Fei Wenxiu

Several years ago, there were the "Three Little Ones" in Shanghai, who were quite famous in society. Among them, "Little Rascal" Ye Zhongfang was the most well-known. Recently, the "Three Little Ones" have rarely been seen, each pursuing their own future endeavors. Unexpectedly, "Little Rascal" Ye Zhongfang has ended up in court due to his love for Chen Xiuzhen (also known as Shirley), a dance hall girl. Here is a record of what I saw at yesterday's trial, in addition to what has already been reported by various newspapers.

Zhao Guangzu Attends the Hearing　Zhao Guangzu, who was once romantically involved with a prostitute named Mei Fei and faced divorce proceedings initiated by his wife, Tan Meiying, but eventually reconciled with his wife, attended the court hearing as a close friend of Ye. Afterwards, Zhao remarked to others, "Today's dance girls only love money and have no affection." Perhaps this was a statement based on his own experiences.

All Court Staff Attended　It happened that there were not many cases at the court on that day. Since many people admired Ye's reputation, they all came to observe the hearing. The spectacle was no less grand than the Xue Die contract termination case.

Sedative Pills Ineffective　Since the lawsuit involving Chen and Ye arose, Ye has been quite frustrated and reluctant to have a public trial, which would hurt his feelings. Consequently, he changed his name and went into hiding at the Beiping Military Academy. Later, upon reading about the facts of the case in the newspaper and receiving an urgent telegram from his lawyer, Jiang Yiping, he rushed back before the trial. However, Ye still did not want to see Chen and planned to end his life. Twenty minutes before the trial, he swallowed ten Atalin sedative pills, hoping to die on the spot in court. Unexpectedly, the pills not only had no effect, but instead invigorated him, allowing him to say everything he wanted to say. Afterwards, Ye told people that it was because his ancestors were watching over him and secretly protecting him.

Fifteen Yuan Forever Etched in His Heart　On the night Ye and Chen engaged in a physical relationship, Ye only had fifteen yuan left in his pocket. After spending it, his pocket was empty. However, Chen not only did not demand more money from him, but also provided him with tea, meals, and other things. He was deeply moved and believed that she was the only true lover in the world. Thus, he had the idea of living together with her, forming an unbreakable bond.

Deep Affection　After the court hearing, Jiang Yiping advised Ye, saying that based on the current situation, he should wake up to reality. However, Ye replied, "I will always love her. Even if she wants to leave me and go elsewhere, I will never stop her. I only hope that she cherishes her future and does not marry the wrong person. Then, even if I wander in a foreign land, I will die with peace of mind."

Singing and Dancing Madly Before Death　Before the trial, Ye, having resolved to die, opened bottles of champagne at the Black Cat dance hall the night before, reveling in extreme pleasure for one last time. It is said that he spent two or three hundred yuan in one night, which shows how heartbroken he was, not caring about money at all.

The Tinder of the Lawsuit　Chen received favorable treatment after entering Ye's residence. Even the first wife addressed her as "sister," and Ye's mother called her "Miss." One day, when the cook served a meal, Chen complained about the taste and suggested to Ye that he dismiss the cook. Ye's mother said, "The world is changing for the worse. A new cook is not as good as an experienced one." Chen thought this meant they valued the cook more than her, so she angrily left and never returned, eventually leading to the lawsuit. The cook can be said to have been the tinder that ignited the conflict.

Travel Notes from India (33) 123

— Linghua

On the 18th, following instructions from Professor Ma Shida, I started using body oil. This oil seems to be ordinary oil, the kind that can be bought at various snack shops, mixed with a type of medicine. This medicine is called Camphor in English and Gobao in the local Hindi dialect. It's the same as Chinese camphor. Adding peppercorns allows it to be stored in cookies. Camphor oil can be applied to various parts of the body to remove dampness and treat all kinds of skin diseases. This is because the area is very humid and hot. Even in winter, the nights are slightly chilly, so blankets are needed, but during the day, only light clothing is worn. If you don't take a cool bath for several days, your body will itch. Even now, in winter, I still have heat rash. I've used various expensive medicines, but they haven't been able to eliminate it. It itches every afternoon. Mrs. Lu, the consul's wife, said that when they arrived during the hot season, they had heat rash, and using this medicine was very effective in clearing it up and providing a cooling sensation. Anyone traveling to India should pay attention to this matter, as it's quite important. It can also ward off foul odors. Chinese camphor comes from Jiangxi and Fujian. Years ago, when I was traveling north from Shaoguan, I saw many camphor trees along the road. A friend from Jiangxi told me that this tree can be boiled to produce camphor, which is extremely profitable. The method is simple. Use a machine to produce it. A capital of over 100,000 is enough. Currently, the Japanese dominate this industry. Camphor trees grow in near-tropical regions, and people who come to hot regions also need to use it. I've only recently begun to understand the strangeness of life in India and realized the need for what the Lotus Sutra says: "Apply oil to your feet." It's essential here to apply oil to your body and feet. Indians have various ways of applying it, with different colors and medicines. They might apply it to their foreheads in various shapes and walk around openly. Over time, this has become a religious custom. The way Burmese women apply makeup to their faces is similar. It's a necessity for living in tropical regions.

On the 20th, Master Daokai and I visited the Asiatic Society on Park Road. A Tibetan man led the tour. Since the Lunar New Year was approaching and there were few people working, there were few visitors. The nature of this society is that it is a public organization for the study of Asian cultures, but in reality, it has become economically controlled by the British government. The director is Dutch. He serves as the secretary. Below him, each country has a representative. They collect documents, pictures, and artifacts from various countries for research. Ancient and modern texts are classified and arranged. The bookshelves are all made of iron, not wooden boxes. Tropical climates require good ventilation. The layout is generally like this. I glanced through it briefly and saw that they had Chinese classics, Taoist scriptures, and Buddhist texts. The Tibetan man showed me mostly about the Tibetan section. The Tibetan man was named Jumyang. He was bald and wore a purple mandarin jacket and robe. Master Dao said that this was the clothing of Buddhist monks. He showed me Tibetan alphabets and phonology. When I read them, they were exactly the same as the four-character rhymes in Chinese. I realized that the study of phonetics and pronunciation with fanqie (a method of indicating the pronunciation of a Chinese character by using two other characters) came to China from India. The Japanese monk Kukai created the Iroha alphabet, also modeled after Indian writing. Tibetan writing is the same. The Mongols also imitated Tibetan writing. Mongols who want to become famous monks must send people to study in Tibet. So, in the realm of sound, India is the great master of Asia. Professor Ma Shida once told me that ancient Indian culture owes much to the power of Krishna. In the Indian language, Krishna is the same word that Jews use for Jesus, Christ. It's the same word, with different long and short sounds. I don't know if they have the same origin.

Reading various English survey reports on Tibet, I sighed at the British audacity in plotting for Tibet. It's not accidental. They have specialists surveying the entire and partial divisions of Tibet. There's a large English-Tibetan dictionary worth 32 rupees. There are thick reports from 1922, 1923, and 1924, published in London, with various illustrations. They record the ethnic customs, products, and everything else in detail, leaving nothing out. We know nothing about this. Even our famous scholars and great politicians know nothing about it. What do we rely on to compete with others? I remember someone once commenting that the Chinese understanding of themselves is far inferior to the foreigners' understanding of us. These are truly heartbreaking words. However, there is a reason for this. The Chinese ignorance of long-term strategies is due to two reasons: one, because we don't know ourselves domestically, let alone know the outside world; two, because the people of a monarchy for thousands of years have no habit of uniting, and there are few independent initiatives in society, lacking the ability to organize and manage society; and three, there is no government assistance or subsidies. It has been 20 years since the revolution. The amount of money spent on wars by the various provincial governments is immeasurable. Has any of it been used to reward academic research and inventions? Alas, there is no talent or common sense in the provincial governments.

Gold Market Turns Downward

Plummeting Over Ten Taels　Yesterday, the 23rd, the gold market once again trended downwards, with rapid fluctuations. The overall movement was not insignificant. A total of fourteen taels were traded throughout the day, ultimately dropping by more than ten taels. This was a reaction after successive increases. The volume of trading in the market was not as high as the previous day, with sellers generally dominating. The situation was the opposite of the previous day, likely due to a slight decrease in foreign exchange rates, causing the domestic market to weaken. The peers' intentions were generally peaceful, and they were not moved by reports of falling prices in overseas silver markets, as European buyers remained strong. Therefore, the gold price dropped early in the morning, running counter to expectations. Later, buyers became aggressive, briefly pushing past the 740 tael mark. However, due to the active selling by Guangdong merchants and large investors, and with the remittance market turning unfavorable, the price suddenly dropped sharply by ten taels. The market stabilized and then weakened again. The British exchange rate continued to decline, and with the Indian exchange rate rising, sellers appeared like clouds on the trading floor, causing the price to fall further. Cotton Market Downturn Begins 131

The cotton market has turned weak, with a slight downturn emerging. This is mainly due to American and Indian cotton prices declining, leading to widespread pessimism and a lack of market confidence. However, gold prices remain strong, so Japanese merchants are still holding tightly. Actual sales to manufacturers are noticeably sluggish, with some selling off their holdings. Nevertheless, due to the high gold prices, foreign cotton still cannot be imported. Domestic cotton stocks from all sources are depleted, and inventory in local warehouses is low. Therefore, the cotton market situation is unusually complex. Although prices are high, foreign cotton cannot be imported, and there is concern that a major collapse may occur in the future.

September: 125.40, down 2.50

October: 124.30, down 2.50

Also, the Osaka spot yarn prices are telegraphed as follows: 20-count Blue Fish: 140 yuan, down 3 yuan, equivalent to 227.9 taels in Shanghai Standard; 20-count Red God of Wealth: 136 yuan, down 2 yuan, equivalent to 221.3 taels in Shanghai Standard; 16-count Fukushima: 133 yuan, down 1 yuan, equivalent to 216.5 taels in Shanghai Standard; 16-count Three Horses: 133 yuan, down 1 yuan, equivalent to 216.5 taels in Shanghai Standard.

Grains, Rice Market Continues Weak 137

Zhabei: Yesterday, twenty to thirty boats arrived from various routes. Sales were extremely slow in the morning. High and low grades of northern japonica rice continued to weaken slightly, mainly due to a lack of inquiries. However, after the market closed, the weather suddenly turned overcast and rainy, so the overall trend seemed to stabilize. Early indica rice arrivals were sparse and sales were dull, with the market softening slightly. Yangxian rice sales were mediocre, with high grades extremely scarce. Trade in medium and lower grades was light, and the market weakened, with little change in the overall price. Duzi xian and local xian rice also experienced sluggish buying interest, with the situation showing weakness within stability. Baiyuan sales were not developing, but prices remained stable at their low levels.

Hunan: Yesterday, over ten boats arrived from the interior. Sales in this area were poor. In the early morning, various mechanically milled japonica rice were mostly quoted down by about one jiao. By noon, the market stabilized slightly due to rain, but transactions were still lackluster. Southern early indica rice was weak and lacked spirit, with only high-grade rice showing some activity, with prices showing little change. Yangdu and Jianlai rice arrivals were scarce and sales were slow, with little market fluctuation. The hanging yuan and fan rice markets were dull and lifeless, but fortunately, arrivals were limited, so prices remained unchanged, with top-grade hung hua rice still hovering around the 10 yuan mark.

Guangdong Merchants Search for Keyuan Rice 138

Yesterday, the Keyuan market showed renewed activity. Supplies of Keyuan rice in Shanghai were already scarce. Only the merchants and hoarders still had some inventory. After a search by Guangdong merchants, 750 bags of high-grade Hunan mechanically milled yuan rice were sold at a price of 14.12 yuan. 500 bags of upper-medium grade Jiangxi mechanically milled yuan rice were sold at a price of 13.70 yuan to 13.45 yuan. Prices were better than previous quotations.

Flour Market Stabilizes in the Afternoon 139

Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, prices for all months were quoted down by foreign wheat by approximately three to four jiao, resulting in an unusually sluggish market, down approximately one fen across the board compared to the previous day's close. The situation remained unfavorable. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, it initially stabilized. Later, due to overcast weather and rain, the attitude of inland merchants seemed to recover slightly, and there was increased speculative buying. Therefore, the market seemed to stabilize again. However, actual sales have recently slowed. Quotations in Tianjin are also weakening, and a favorable outlook is unlikely. As a result, the current month fell a small 2.5 li, May fell a large 2.5 li, June and August were unchanged, July fell a small 2.5 li, and September fell a large 2.5 li.

Wheat Market Weak in the Morning, Up in the Afternoon 140

Yesterday, the wheat market was particularly sluggish after opening in the morning. As spot goods for the current month were easily available, the lowest price fell to 3 taels, 9 qian, and 7 fen. Distant months followed suit, falling slightly by three to four fen. However, when the market opened in the afternoon, it was initially sluggish, but later, due to strength in the flour market and rainy weather, external buying interest revived. All months recovered three to four fen from their lowest prices. However, current wheat stocks in all warehouses are reportedly ample, and further gains are unlikely. As a result, the current month was unchanged, May rose a large 1 fen, June was unchanged, July rose a large 1 fen, August rose a small 1 fen, and September rose a small 2 fen.

Sugar Market: Japanese Sugar Opens at 20,000 Bags 141

Yesterday, sugar market reports from production areas indicated that Cuban spot sugar remained unchanged. New York sugar futures rose by two points for all months. Java spot and futures also remained unchanged. In the Public Association market, Dutch sugar #24 coarse white was relatively strong, with transactions still at 10.05 taels, and several thousand bags were traded. The market remained stable. Medium white was at 10 taels, #18 was at 9.9 taels, with very little activity. The rotation of Japanese sugar from the factory’s Meiji telegraph has changed. The price for 10,000 bags of delivery in May and June was 4.40 Japanese yen plus tax. At the same time, Minghua Sugar also opened with 10,000 bags, with delivery in May at 6.50 Japanese yen including tax. Because the two goods were tied together, the firms were still keen to import. Spot trading was rather quiet. YT brand was at 10.045 taels, YRO brand was at 9.925 taels, N brand was at 10.0525 taels, HS brand was at 10.015 taels. The market was generally flat. The Huaxin brand opened with over one thousand bags of spot blue sugar at 8 taels, but the market was flat. Domestic produced Banan Qing opened with 300-odd bags at 7.5 taels, up one qian from the previous market, and the brand owners were holding on tightly. Thus, the market appeared quite lively.

Dried and Sundry Goods: Hunan Lotus Seeds Slow Sales, Market Flat 142

Recent arrivals of Hunan lotus seeds have been scarce. The Hankow market is flat. Top and middle grades are priced at 17.7 taels per dan, and Chang lotus seeds are priced at around 16 taels. Lower grades vary. Shanghai’s stock on hand is not particularly high. However, due to mediocre sales, prices have been difficult to increase. Only Ningbo’s buying interest is slightly better. There have been some sporadic transactions in this area. Yesterday’s market priced top-grade Xiangtan lotus seeds at 37-38 taels. Raozhou and Hengzhou lotus seeds sold for 32-33 taels. Tianjin gang lotus seeds sold for 29-30 taels. Changde lotus seeds sold for 28 taels.

Silk and Tea: Douppion Silk Price Rises Ten Taels 143

The meteoric rise of the Douppion silk market this year has broken all previous records since the inception of Douppion silk. With strong sales of silk fabrics, Douppion silk is trending strong. With limited raw material supply, the price of Douppion cocoons is rising. As Douppion silk goods are in short supply and high demand, prices have risen sharply. Yesterday, Hangzhou silk merchants purchased 30 bales of Grade A Douppion silk at 730 taels, up another 10 taels from before.

Hardware: Black Iron Sheet and English Steel Plate Both Rise 144

Yesterday’s hardware transactions were brisk for out-of-town merchants but sluggish for local merchants. Therefore, export goods were quite lively. However, factory orders seemed quiet. Due to prior contractions, the prices of various goods were trending upwards, especially for black iron sheet and English steel plate. 18-gauge black iron sheet rose sharply by 2-3 qian yesterday, opening at 11.3 taels per dan, with 600-700 dan traded. Most buyers were from Tianjin. Merchants from Qingdao and Yantai also made some spot purchases. It is reported that many inland merchants have recently been inquiring. Given the limited inventory in Shanghai, the current market appears to have insufficient supply. English steel plate prices have been gradually increasing overseas recently, but arrivals have been very limited, so inventory is not large, and confidence is relatively good. Standards are therefore trending upwards. Export merchants from Tianjin, Yantai, Qingdao, etc., have also been buying more recently, and spot goods are becoming increasingly scarce. Prices are steadily increasing. Currently, 2.5 li is estimated at 9.25 taels per dan, 0.5 fen is at 7 taels, 7 li is at 6.75 taels, 1 fen is at 6.5 taels, and above 1.5 fen is estimated at 6.25 taels, up 2-4 qian from before.

Europe and Asia 146

Aviation Aircraft Arrives in Shanghai

Through Flight from Manchuria Yesterday

Carrying 75 Kilograms of Mail

Not Via Kulun, but Via Linxi

Arrives in Shanghai on the 3rd. The Europe Asia Airlines began trial through-flights from Shanghai to Manchuria on the 19th, carrying mail for free, limited to 75 kilograms per item. Each item can carry 25 copies of newspapers directly to the destination, also free of charge. The Europe Asia Flight No. 3, flying from Manchuria to Beijing, was scheduled to depart Manchuria on the 21st, but due to a Siberian train delay, it was delayed until the 22nd to fly to Beijing. Yesterday afternoon at about 3 p.m. it flew from Beijing to Shanghai, carrying a large bag of mail, totaling 75 kilograms. The mail consisted of items mailed from London on April 9 and 11, from Paris on April 11, from Berlin on April 12, and from Manchuria on April 22. Continued through-flights from Shanghai to Manchuria are scheduled for the 26th, May 3rd and 10th.

Change Via Linxi. The Europe Asia Airlines route was originally planned to go from Shanghai via Nanjing, Jinan, Beiping, Kulun and reach Manchuria. However, the airline has changed its route because the circuitous route to Kulun is inconvenient. After reaching Beiping, the route goes via Linxi and reaches Manchuria.

Tentative Schedule. The airline has now tentatively set its flight schedule, which may be changed when formally launched on May 15th. The schedule is recorded below. Every Friday and Sunday the flight departs Shanghai at 5:00 a.m., arriving in Beijing at 6:45 a.m., departing Beijing at 7:30 a.m., arriving in Ji at 11:15 a.m., departing Ji at noon 12 p.m., arriving in Beiping at 2:30 p.m., departing Beiping at 3 p.m., arriving in Linxi at 6:30 p.m., staying overnight in Linxi, then departing Linxi at 6 a.m. the next morning, arriving in Manchuria at noon 12 p.m. Every Sunday and Tuesday the flight departs Manchuria at 9 a.m. for Shanghai, arriving in Linxi at 3 p.m., departing Linxi at 3:45 p.m., arriving in Beiping at 7:15 p.m., staying overnight in Beiping, then departing Beiping at 4 a.m. the next morning, arriving in Ji at 6:30 a.m., departing Ji at 7:15 a.m., arriving in Beijing at 11 a.m., departing Beijing at 11:45 a.m., arriving in Shanghai at 1:30 p.m.

National Radio Stations 147

Open International Telegrams

Beginning May 15th

The international telegram stations in China that receive and transmit international telegrams are originally Guangdong, Hankou, Shantou, Fuzhou, Shanghai and Xiamen six locations. Recently, with the completion of the China-America, China-Germany and China-France radio stations, there has been an urgent desire to develop communications with the outside world. Yesterday, the Ministry of Communications issued orders that, beginning May 15th, all radio stations across the country should open international telecommunications services. Including Tianjin, Beiping, Nanjing, Yichang, Anqing, Hangzhou, Ningbo, Wuhu, Dinghai, Qingdao, Nanchang, Chongqing, Wanxian, Yantai, and Changsha, there are fifteen locations. The Telecommunications Bureau has also informed the above radio stations, saying "It is decided that beginning May 15th, all radio stations across the country will open international telecommunications services. From now on, as the station's business increases, greater caution should be exercised in handling telegrams to avoid delays."

Hwa Yang Steamer Sinks 148

All Crew and Passengers Rescued

Totaling One Hundred and Fourteen People

Transported to Hong Kong by English Ship

The Hang An Company's Hwa Yang steamer struck a reef at Yushan, Yangnan, Wenzhou. This news has been reported in the newspaper twice. Yesterday, it was heard that the ship was completely sunk due to excessive damage. Fortunately, the crew and passengers were rescued. A detailed account is as follows:

Ship Body Damaged. The Hwa Yang steamer encountered fog at 2:30 p.m. on the 21st, and sailed to 122 degrees 14 minutes east longitude and 28 degrees 51 minutes 30 seconds north latitude, the extreme northwest corner of southern Yushan, ship body hitting a reef in the fog, striking the port side of the ship at 30 degrees. The impact was excessive and immediately ruptured the hull, and seawater rushed into the ship. At this time the ship's captain was very anxious, seeing that the ship would sink immediately, he sailed the ship towards the reef, hoping to beach the ship on the reef to avoid crew and passengers being caught off guard. As a result, the bow drove into the foot of the reef mountain and ran aground, while the stern was in the sea, allowing time to rescue the crew and passengers ashore. It took 24 hours for the ship to sink, but the bottom of the ship was pierced by the reef and the damage was indescribable.

Difficult Rescue. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Gong Ping steamship sailed to Ma'an Island to assist the Hwa Yang. At 5:50 p.m. on the 21st, the seawater had already risen to the deck of the Hwa Yang. The stern was completely submerged, leaving only one hull outside. Crew and passengers were all on southern Yushan. Gong Ping ship released two sampans, the first attempt capsized because of the large north wind waves, the second attempt was also overturned by huge waves, and one of the sampans had its bow broken by waves. One sailor almost lost his life and could not go to the rescue and had to withdraw and wait. The British Company's 16,000-ton giant ship Lagan Pootai arrived, and Gong Ping asked them to help with the rescue.

Crew and Passengers Transported to Hong Kong. The British Company's Lagan Pootai, began to release small sampans into the sea at 3:00 p.m. on the 22nd, after the fog dissipated and the waves settled, to go to southern Yushan to rescue the stranded people on the mountain in batches to its own ship. It took three hours to rescue all 114 crew and passengers. At 7:17 p.m., it left Ma'an Island and went straight to Hong Kong, sending a telegram to Shanghai. A total of 114 passengers and crew of the Hwa Yang ship were rescued at Ma'an Island and have been transported to Hong Kong. According to the Hwa Yang captain, all passengers and crew were rescued safely. Yesterday Hang An Company had translated the telegram and posted it in the office, so that family members of the passengers and crew could come and view it.

Ship Sinks. Yesterday at 11:00 a.m., Hang An Company first received a telegram from the Jianghai Customs Administration's Liujing, stating that the location of the Hwa Yang accident was at the extreme northwest of southern Yushan, the port side had broken and tilted into the sea, and everything from the observation deck to the stern had been completely destroyed and gone. At 12:50 p.m., they received a telegram from the Hwa Yang captain, Shakerov, stating that the ship had sunk and all crew and passengers had been rescued by British ships to Hong Kong. By yesterday afternoon, other than the bow on the reef, which had some traces, everything else had disappeared, with only one mast revealing the sea surface.

Three Ships Return. The rescue ship Gong Ping had already returned to Shanghai yesterday morning. Hang An staff went to the ship to ask about the situation. The captain of Gong Ping said that there was no hope of salvaging the Hwa Yang, that the crew and passengers were unharmed. The company had sent Fushin and Chengli ships to assist in the rescue, but when they were about to reach Ma'an Island, they received a radio message from the English ship stating that the Hwa Yang crew and passengers had been rescued and taken to Hong Kong, so there was no need to go. Therefore, Fushin ship had returned to Shanghai yesterday, and Chengli ship went to Shantou.

Warship to Prevent Theft. The area is frequented by pirates, and any shipwrecks attract them to rob the victims. This time, after the pirates waited for the Hwa Yang passengers to be rescued, they sent ships to southern Yushan to rob. Upon seeing the arrival of Liujing warship, they did not dare board the ship. The Ministry of the Navy also complied with Hang An's request and ordered the Yongji ship stationed in Chuanshan to sail to the area to prevent robbery and plunder. Both warships have arrived in the area to protect it.

Pay off the Crew and Passengers. Upon receiving news of the crew and passengers' rescue, Hang An Company’s manager Huang Xingge sent a radio message to the British ship Lagan Pootai, to be relayed to Chen Youbai, one of the rescued people, instructing him to represent the company, take the 113 rescued people, arrange for food and accommodation after arriving in Hong Kong, and instruct people in Hong Kong to raise funds to buy ship tickets for the rescued passengers going to Fujian and pay for them to return to their hometowns. The other crew members and sailors are asked to find a way to return to Shanghai by ship. The telegram has been sent. Chen Youbai is the shipowner of Fushin and a good friend of Huang Xingge. This time, he was also on the Hwa Yang ship going to Fujian and was also a victim of the shipwreck.

Inform Family Members. Yesterday, Hang An Company had notified the passengers' families of the shipwreck and rescue of crew and passengers. Many of the sailors’ dependents, passengers' relatives, etc., came to the company to inquire. The company immediately showed them the telegrams and waited for the shipowners and crew members to return to Shanghai to inquire about the true story of the accident and the extent of the damage, and then decide whether to salvage it or not. It is still uncertain.

National Government Military Advisor 149

Yang Hu Narrowly Escapes Assassination

Communists Induce Gatekeeper to Murder Yang

Wu Youcai Confesses Unreservedly After Capture

Accomplices Shi Youheng and Three Others Also Arrested

Guowenshe reports that Yang Hu, Military Advisor to the National Government, has been residing on Avenue du Capitaine D'Allonville in the French Concession since retiring from his position as Garrison Commander of Songhu. He seems to be mostly uninvolved with military and political affairs. However, the communists deeply resented Yang's past animosity and plotted to assassinate him. However, Yang's protection was strict, and they could not find an opportunity. Recently, the gatekeeper employed at Yang's residence was induced to join the Communist Party, and the matter of assassinating Yang occurred. Fortunately, it was discovered early, and he escaped harm. The assassination plot is summarized below.

Regular Precautions. Yang Hu, also known as Xiaotian, is from Ningguo, Anhui Province. He initially followed Sun Yat-sen to engage in revolution, experiencing great hardship. After the National Revolutionary Army established its position in Jiangsu and Zhejiang, Chairman Chiang appointed Yang as the Garrison Commander of Songhu. Shortly after, the split between Nanjing and Wuhan occurred, and Yang deeply hated the communists, vowing to eliminate them. The communists at that time hated Yang as if he were a thorn in their side. Therefore, in recent years, Yang's precautions have been stringent. Every time Yang went out, in addition to hiring guards, he also carried two revolvers to defend himself against harm from villains.

The Bandits Cannot Take Advantage. The bandits saw that Yang's precautions were strict and could not find an opportunity. They changed their strategy, planning to induce those close to him and bribe them with huge sums of money to kill Yang in the interim. Therefore, the communist party has been unusually active recently and has been paying close attention to Yang. It is rumored that the party recently had the slogan "If Yang is not removed, the Communist Party will never be able to do as it pleases." They tried every means, and Yang's gatekeeper, Wu Youcai, a native of Jiangpu, was induced to join the Communist Party to assist them. However, Heaven's net is vast, and the matter was discovered by the Yang family's servants, who immediately ordered the Municipal Public Security Bureau to send police to arrest him. He surrendered on the 21st of this month.

The Case is Solved. Since Wu Youcai started working at Yang's residence, he has been diligent and cautious, and he has not gone out except during work hours. Therefore, Yang regarded Wu Youcai very highly and praised him repeatedly. Recently, Wu changed his behavior. When he went out, he did not return all night. When asked where he went, he gave vague answers. The family members felt that the gatekeeper's responsibility was related to the safety of the entire family. Even if there was an accident, he would not return in the middle of the night, and there was no one to answer the door. Therefore, suspicion arose. One day, Wu was seen going out, and personnel were secretly sent to follow him. Later, because his actions were suspicious, with the suspicion that he was meeting with bandits, they reported it to Yang, who sent a letter to the Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Chen Xizeng, asking him to send police to arrest Wu. He was arrested on the 21st and taken to the bureau for interrogation.

Confesses to Assassination. After Wu was arrested on the 21st, the Public Security Bureau added to the interrogation, as the case was related to harming important party and government figures. As a result, Wu also knew that he could not hide it and revealed everything. The most important point in his confession was "After I joined the Communist Party, the accomplices wanted to kill Yang, but they could not succeed due to his strict protection. Recently, I received orders from the communists to assassinate Yang." At the same time, after several detailed inquiries, he also implicated accomplices Shi Youheng, Zhu Lianxiang, Luo Qiting, etc., who have also been arrested. The bureau is currently interrogating them and is strictly pursuing other remaining accomplices.

Directorate-General of Budget, Ministry of Industries, and Bureau of Social Affairs 152

Joint Shanghai Industrial Survey

To Commence Regionally on May 1st

Aims to Clarify the Status of Industry

The Statistics Bureau of the National Government's Directorate-General of Budget plans to conduct a national industrial census, with a set procedure starting in Shanghai. Simultaneously, the Ministry of Industries intends to survey specific industries in Shanghai. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs, noting significant changes since the last industrial survey, also plans a follow-up investigation. Therefore, at the Statistics Bureau's suggestion, the two agencies will use the same forms and conduct the surveys concurrently. This will spare factories the burden of repeated surveys and achieve twice the results with half the effort for the government. After drafting the plan, the National Chiao Tung University Research Institute and economics students also sought to participate, as they had a project to collaboratively study the transportation of industrial goods and the competition between domestic and foreign goods. They planned a survey, and now the three agencies and two academic groups have jointly established the Shanghai Industrial Survey Joint Office. Zhang Zongbi, a staff member from the Statistics Bureau, has been appointed as the survey director, and over ten staff members from the various agencies and groups, including Lin Mingqi, will serve as surveyors. Starting on the 27th of this month, they will first visit major factories, and from May 1st, a general survey will be conducted regionally. All surveyors will be issued special survey certificates with their half-body photo attached and stamped with the official seal of the Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs for identification. However, fearing that factories may not be fully aware or understand the survey's purpose and methods, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has been notified to inform member factories and trade associations, clarifying that this joint survey of Shanghai factories aims to understand the position of domestic industry in order to find ways to promote and protect it, with no other purpose. They hope that factories will provide accurate and detailed information without hesitation.

Municipal Health Bureau 160

Administering Cholera Vaccinations Early

Those Wishing to be Vaccinated May Write to the Bureau

In light of the fact that over 300,000 people received free cholera vaccinations last summer, but a few genuine cases of cholera were still discovered, the Municipal Health Bureau, in order to prevent future occurrences, has begun administering vaccinations earlier this year. It has hired doctors, nurses, medical students, and existing staff to carry out this work. Starting on May 1st, personnel will be dispatched to schools throughout the city to vaccinate all students. After completion, personnel will be successively dispatched to shantytowns, boat-dwelling communities, factories, government agencies, organizations, and densely populated residential areas to administer vaccinations day and night. At the same time, hundreds of thousands of propaganda materials are being prepared for distribution. If any organization with more than 30 people wishes to be vaccinated against cholera in advance, they may write directly to the bureau requesting a vaccination, and personnel will be dispatched on a scheduled basis.

Minutes of the Executive Committee of the Children's Welfare Association 161

Children's Day Application Approved

Children's Welfare Garden Now Open

The monthly standing committee meeting of the Executive Committee of the Chinese Children's Welfare Association was held last Saturday at the boardroom of the National Products Bank. As the association's chairman, Dr. Kong Yongzhi, had important official business and could not attend, the meeting was chaired by Judge Hu Yigu. Dr. Niu Huisheng reported on the achievements of the two healthcare clinics, Mr. Li Daonan reported on the economic situation, and General Secretary Wu Weide reported on the progress of promoting the 4/4 Children's Day, stating that Chairman Jiang of the National Government had instructed the Executive Yuan to take note of the matter. In addition to the reports, there were several important discussions. The most noteworthy of these was the Children's Welfare Garden, jointly operated by the association and Shanghai University. The garden is located in the Hudong Commune of Yangshupu and specializes in caring for the young children of factory women. It is a daycare center and opened on April 20th. Professor Chen Heqin has been appointed as the honorary director, Mrs. Hai Mu Hua as the honorary head, and Mrs. Wang Guanyi as a teacher. She studied at Ningbo Chongde Girls' School and Taizhou Meide Girls' School, graduated from Shanghai Guangren Hospital, and holds a certificate from the Chinese Nurses Association. The garden is said to both care for the children of factory workers and conduct experiments to study the physiological, psychological, and educational development of children, as well as their family environment. Dr. Sun Keji, a gynecologist, Dr. Fu Wenshou, a pediatrician, Dr. Wang Zonghai, Professor Chen Heqin, and Ms. Wu Zhou Shujing have been specially invited to conduct research and investigations.

Customs Brokerage Industry Labor Dispute 162

Bureau of Social Affairs Conducted Final Mediation Yesterday

Parties Insisted on Negotiations Until 8 PM with No Results

Over Two Hundred Workers Marched to the Municipal Party Headquarters to Petition

Due to the fact that the Shanghai customs brokerage workers' strike, the customs brokerage industry association, and the cotton cloth industry association have not reached a concrete solution through negotiations, the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs convened another mediation yesterday to expedite a resolution. The meeting continued until evening, but the issue of customs inspection fees could not be resolved due to the parties' insistence, so it was adjourned. The parties will deliberate on their own before a decision is made, and the three associations will hold a general meeting today to discuss the matter. Yesterday, workers went to the Municipal Party Headquarters to petition. The details are as follows:

Workers' Petition: Over two hundred members of the Customs Brokerage Workers' Union marched to the Municipal Party Headquarters to petition at 11:00 AM yesterday. The march was led by Wang Huihe and Cheng Pinshun, with Zhang Yusheng and Bi Nanshan serving as marshals. They carried small white bamboo cloth petition flags and wore petition bamboo cloth symbols bearing the union's seal for identification. Their demands were: (1) Regarding the cotton cloth transportation fee case at our factory, please send a letter to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs requesting enforcement of the previously issued Notice No. 9097. (2) The opening of the docks concerns the issue of Western and Eastern goods and is not related to cotton cloth at our factory, so it cannot be combined. Chen Junyi, a standing committee member of the Civil Training Association, instructed staff member Zhu Yakui to receive the petitioners. Due to the large number of workers, it was inconvenient to inquire, so he ordered the appointment of representatives to proceed. Subsequently, Sun Liansheng, Fang Pinghe, Su Houxin, and He Xixiang were appointed as representatives. As a result, the workers' demands were accepted, and they were promised that personnel would be dispatched immediately to mediate with the Bureau of Social Affairs. Thereupon, all the workers, feeling satisfied, returned to their union.

Mediation Process: At 2:00 PM yesterday, the Bureau of Social Affairs convened representatives from the Customs Brokerage Association, the Cotton Market Association, and the Customs Brokerage Workers' Union to mediate. Present were Chen Songyuan and Ke Ganchen, representatives from the Cotton Cloth Industry Association; Shi Zhikun and Zhu Xieshen, representatives from the Customs Brokerage Association; and Su Houxin and Ren Xixiang, representatives from the Customs Brokerage Workers' Union. Guo Yongxi of the Bureau of Social Affairs presided over the meeting, and Jiang Shifu served as the recorder. The chairman began by stating that the cause of the dispute was the Cotton Cloth Industry Association's decision that the transportation fees for customs brokerage should be borne by the merchants themselves, which led to opposition from the Workers' Union. The bureau had convened mediation previously, but it was shelved because the two sides had requested to settle the matter privately outside the meeting. It was reported that the matter had not been resolved to date, so the representatives were convened again for discussion. He also stated that the Cotton Cloth Industry Association had previously agreed to add two dimes for transportation, regardless of the distance, but the Customs Brokerage had not agreed. In the chairman's opinion, if a contract were not established now, it would likely cause future disturbances. He asked the representatives for their opinions. Next, the representatives expressed their opinions. The Customs Brokerage Association's representatives stated that they were willing to negotiate as long as their industry did not suffer any losses. The Cotton Cloth Association's representatives believed that the transportation fee issue was entirely the responsibility of the merchants and should be collected directly from the merchants by the Workers' Union and should not be borne by their industry. Furthermore, the various terms had been roughly agreed upon at the previous meeting at the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, but the Customs Brokerage Association had failed to acknowledge them at the time. Regarding the issue of losses, the answer could be simply that the Customs Brokerage industry pays wages to its workers and the Cotton Cloth industry should not be responsible for transportation fees. Furthermore, the association represents over two hundred companies and is not limited to cotton cloth (meaning it is not limited to domestic cloth). The chairman then stated that this case could be considered a commercial dispute and not a labor-management dispute. The Customs Brokerage Association could not shirk its responsibility and hoped that the parties could understand each other. He then inquired about the representatives' positions on the transportation fee issue: (1) The Workers' Union representatives proposed that for the three docks, Osaka, Huangpu, and the Warehouse, each transportation trip should be uniformly five dimes. (2) The Customs Brokerage Association proposed that the new docks, such as Gonghexing and Huishan, should also be included in the calculation. At this point, the chairman convened individual talks with representatives from the three parties for questions and explanation. After the questions, they first discussed the second dock issue proposed by the Cotton Cloth Association. They proposed that for the four docks, Osaka, Huangpu, the Warehouse, and Huishan, the Cotton Cloth industry would pay 2.5 dimes and the Customs Brokerage Association would pay 1.5 dimes, totaling four dimes. However, as the Customs Brokerage Association did not agree, it was temporarily put aside. Then, they discussed the terms and the customs inspection fee issue. Because the two sides argued fiercely and could not resolve the matter, the meeting was adjourned. A decision will be made after each side has considered the matter further.

Jinxin Factory Labor Dispute Resolved Yesterday 163

The labor strike at the Jinxin Silk Weaving Factory on Avenue du Lieutenant Petiot in the French Concession had lasted for over thirty days. The Bureau of Social Affairs had mediated six times, but the company refused to reinstate Sun Maoer and five others and denied wages for the strike period, resulting in a failed mediation. Yesterday, the municipal government convened an arbitration committee, and the arbitration resulted in: (1) Wages to be paid as usual for Dr. Sun Yat-sen's Memorial Day. (2) Sun Maoer and five others to be allowed to return to work. (3) A subsidy of ten yuan per person for meals during the strike period. The labor side was satisfied. The members of the labor union were summoned to have a general meeting on Monday to resume work. However, Sun Maoer's injuries are severe, and he may not be able to work for a while. The Special District Court held a hearing yesterday. The defendant was not present, and the plaintiff Sun Maoer appeared in court, despite being ill. The judge questioned him about the assault and the doctor examined his injuries. The hearing was scheduled for Thursday.

Issues Before the Opening of the Sanxin Cotton Mill 164

Over Four Thousand Veteran Workers Requesting Re-Employment

After the new owner of the Sanxin Cotton Mill on Yangshupu Road, General Manager Rong Zongjing, took over, he appointed Wu Kunsheng as the factory manager and Wu Tuhuai and Wang Shizhang as the chief and assistant engineers, respectively. The handover has now been completed, and it was announced that the factory would reopen on the 27th of this month, with worker registration beginning on the 21st. All the veteran workers immediately went to register. Because the factory required that the registration procedures be conducted with a new employee as an introducer, over four thousand veteran workers became alarmed and sent representatives, Tian Sanzi and Hou Jiahai, to the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs yesterday to petition, requesting that the factory comply with the previous agreement to re-employ them and not refuse work. The bureau dispatched personnel to investigate and verify the matter for further action.

French Concession Issues This Year's Public Bonds 166

Totaling One and a Half Million Taels

The Director-General of the French Municipal Council, Fuller, issued a notice yesterday regarding the solicitation of public bonds, stating that the council plans to issue 1931 public bonds totaling one and a half million taels, divided into fifteen thousand shares with a face value of one hundred taels each. The regulations for the issuance of these public bonds are hereby announced for general knowledge. (1) Each share of this public bond will be sold at face value and fully redeemed at maturity, from August 31, 1941, to August 31, 1956. During this period, the council may redeem all or part of the public bonds after giving six months' prior notice in the council's gazette and major newspapers in Shanghai. (2) The annual interest rate for this public bond is six percent, calculated from the date of purchase. The first interest payment date is scheduled for February 28, 1932. Interest will be paid semi-annually on February 28th and August 31st of each year. The council will send the interest receipt to the bondholder for each interest period. (3) This public bond can be transferred, but the recipient must register with the council to be valid. (4) The council uses all properties and taxes of the Shanghai French Concession to guarantee the repayment of principal and interest on these bonds, except for the public bonds issued in the years 1902, 1911, 1914, 1915, 1916, 1921, 1922, 1924, 1925, 1926, 1928, 1929, and 1930. (5) The Municipal Council's General Office will begin receiving bond purchase applications from April 21, 1931.

Transport Fee for Silver Dollars to Increase by 20% 168

To Be Increased from May 1st

The silver and cash industries in Shanghai have historically contracted land transport of silver dollars to Da Feng (Jing-Hu Railway) and Tong He (Hu-Hang-Yong Railway) companies. This time, due to the railway authorities' decision to increase passenger and freight fares uniformly by 20%, the companies sent letters stating that silver dollars should not be treated the same as passengers and freight and requested an exemption. Subsequently, they received approval to temporarily exempt the silver dollar transport fee pending further instructions from the Ministry of Railways to the railway authorities. Now, the Department of Railways has issued instructions from the Ministry of Railways (Number: Ye Zi 10995), stating that the current rates may be temporarily maintained, but starting May 1st, transport fees will be uniformly collected at the increased rate of 20%. All banks and money houses must be officially notified, and their subordinates must comply. After receiving the letter from the two companies, the Money Trade Association recorded the official letter and the Ministry of Railways' instructions for the market so that all members would know what to do.

Letter from the Anti-Opium Society to Organizational Groups 170

The Bai Case is Entirely False Accusations

Earnestly Hoping for Strong Support

Bai Zhiying, the wife of Huang Jiawei, General Secretary of the Chinese National Anti-Opium Society, has been falsely accused of trafficking morphine and was investigated by the Hong Kong Customs. The matter has been proven untrue by Huang and his wife, the society's standing committee, the municipal party headquarters, and the Hong Kong Customs. The rumors are baseless. These details have been reported previously. The society is deeply concerned that the accusers will not succeed in their defamation and will continue to implement plans to sabotage the society, which is very important to the future of the Anti-Opium movement. They sent letters to the associated groups of the society, asking them to uphold justice and provide practical assistance. The original letter is recorded as follows: Respected Sirs, Some time ago, the society's General Secretary Huang Jiawei and his wife, Ms. Bai Zhiying, went to Taiwan to inspect the opium ban. Suddenly, it was falsely alleged that Ms. Huang trafficked morphine and was investigated by the Hong Kong Customs. The news spread widely, and all circles at home and abroad paid close attention. Huang and his wife submitted counter-evidence, and the society's standing committee and various party headquarters thoroughly investigated the matter and declared it to be untrue. Recently, the Hong Kong Customs also proved that it was completely unfounded. All of this has been disclosed in the newspapers. Huang worked hard to combat opium and was falsely accused. All comrades feel injustice. The society has drafted the following response: (1) Please ask the authorities to severely punish the person who fabricated the rumors and accusations and impose the penalty for false accusations. (2) Write to the Chinese and foreign newspapers to uphold justice based on the facts and clear the names of Mr. Huang and his wife. (3) Send telegrams to anti-opium groups in the various local branches nationwide to clarify the facts for Mr. Huang and his wife to dispel doubts and clarify the truth. Your Society has always sympathized with opium and has been especially concerned about the Society. Apart from actively handling the above-mentioned matters, we also hope that you will uphold justice to correct public opinion and maintain the anti-opium movement. It is expected that the other party's conspiracy will not succeed and will continue to carry out various acts of sabotage against the Society. It is hoped that all parties will understand the situation and provide spiritual and practical support. The future of the society depends on it. We hereby inform you. Respectfully yours, The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society.

Shanghai Western Medicine Joint Conference 171

Held Yesterday at the Public Charity Hospital

The Shanghai Western Medicine Society held a joint conference yesterday afternoon at 6:00 PM at the Public Charity Hospital. Dozens of Chinese and foreign male and female doctors attended and presented difficult and complicated cases received during the year for discussion to study treatment methods. The case presented by Dr. Gao Enqi concerned a girl who was only fourteen months old with one less long bone in her lower left leg. Normally, there are always two long bones in each lower leg, but she was missing one. She will inevitably face some inconvenience in walking. Dr. Gao also stated that according to reports, there are only about three hundred cases of this disease worldwide. A renowned New York surgeon had successfully treated one case with bone grafting, but there are no other records in medical books. Many other difficult cases were presented by Chinese and foreign doctors. In addition to explaining the conditions, they also showed X-ray photos. The meeting lasted approximately two hours and then adjourned.

Jiangda Paddle Wheel Damaged 172

Must Be Repaired Before Sailing

The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Jiangda Steamer, which arrived in Shanghai from the Yangtze River, collided with River Buoy No. 4 when entering the Huangpu River. Fortunately, the captain steered hard to avoid it. The left paddle wheel of the Jiangda Steamer had already struck the river buoy. After arriving in Shanghai, Chen Yao, an engineer from the company, inspected it and found that three-quarters of the steamer's left paddle wheel was broken. It has been reported to the shipping department and must be repaired before it can sail.

Local News Two

The Dazzling Municipal 179

Gaoqiao Public Bus

Yesterday's test drive circled various places

Today it will be transported to Gaoqiao to run

After the municipal government-operated Pujiang ferry set sail to Gaoqiao, the Municipal Public Works Bureau also planned to establish public buses in the area, to connect water and land transportation, so as to facilitate travelers. The bus has been completed in the past few days.

Its structure is approximately 5.4 meters long, 2.05 meters wide, and 2.3 meters high, accommodating 35 people per vehicle. The passenger seats are in two rows, all using spring cushions and horsehair backrests. There are 24 glass windows, all equipped with hand-cranked lifts. The car roof is equipped with five electric lights and two ventilators. The car's exterior is painted white on top and yellow on the bottom, dazzling and extremely magnificent. yesterday

Yesterday's Test Drive of the Gaoqiao Public Bus 180

Held a test drive. Guests who arrived successively included various counselors, secretaries, section chiefs of the municipal government, and other bureau secretaries, section chiefs, district chiefs of the Public Security Bureau, managers of the municipal bank, etc. In addition, representatives from tram, public bus, and long-distance bus companies also participated. At 2 p.m., it departed from the memorial tower of Mr. Chen YingShi in the old Ximen, heading south, smooth and fast, bright windows and soft cushions, extremely comfortable, all passengers expressed satisfaction. Passing through Zhonghua Road, Guohuo Road, circling the outer Malu, Dongmen Road, turning from Minguo Road into Avenue Edward VII, then following Sichuan Road, North Sichuan Road, and heading towards Baoshan Road Tiantong Lane, heading east to the Bund, and finally following Nanjing Road to Weihaiwei Road Zhongshemen, stopped abruptly. Secretary Yuanfang Xu of the Public Works Bureau and Section Chief Boying Tan welcomed the guests into the room

Held a tea party. During the meeting, Secretary Xu announced the process of establishing the Gaoqiao public bus and hoped that those present would support it to facilitate its progress. The conversation lasted about half an hour, and everyone dispersed happily. As for the bus, it is said that it will be transported to Pudong this morning to officially start running, and the two buses previously rented from the Huashang Public Bus Company will be completely returned.
