American Sailor 182

Shoots and Kills a Worker

American Sailor Has No Gun License

Shooting and Killing People While Blaming Being Beaten

The Deceased's Brother Will File a Lawsuit

The Western-style house at 15 Fair Road, Broadway Road, Hongkou, is owned by Zhu Shichang. Recently, the house was damaged, and Zhu hired nine workers, including Gu Jingen "30 years old", Chen Guiqing, etc., to repair it. It has been many days. Suddenly, a tragedy occurred at around half past midnight yesterday morning. The workers suddenly had a verbal dispute with the American sailor and Ms. Si (transliteration) living on the second floor of the house, and immediately opened fire with a pistol, causing Gu Jingen to be seriously injured and killed on the spot. The Huishan Patrol Station in charge of the area ordered detectives to investigate and brought the body to the Fellen Road autopsy station. Yesterday morning, Guo Huaipu, the prosecutor of the Special District Court, was commissioned to the institute. Under examination, he ascended to the case. According to the complaint from witness Chen Guiqing and others, we have been working inside for four or five days and staying inside at night. Last night, we were talking when the Westerner and Ms. Si came and said a few words to us in Western language. Because we don't understand Western language, we don't know what they said. So they closed the room tightly, and immediately shot into the door with a pistol outside the door, about eight or nine shots. Gu was shot and killed. But Ms. Si confessed that I and my wife were asleep that night, and suddenly heard someone opening the door of the bathroom. My wife was quite surprised, so she went to the worker and surrounded me and beat me. Then they closed the door, and I went to get a pistol. They knew it and ran out again, and beat me fiercely again. For self-defense, I fired a shot, not as many as nine shots. Mr. Guo asked if his pistol had a license. He replied that this gun was brought to Shanghai from the United States five years ago and has not been registered. Then Gu Lu, the widow of the deceased, complained that there was a four-year-old son and a ten-year-old daughter in the family, and no one to support them. She asked for a pension. However, Gu Awu, the brother of the deceased, said that he did not want to receive a pension and had to file a lawsuit with the governing office. Mr. Guo then ruled that Gu Jingen, the deceased, was shot and killed by the Westerner and Ms. Si. The body was allowed to be buried by his wife Gu Lu after signing a settlement.

The "Ta Mei Evening News" said that Qiu Fushi, a mechanic from the American Yangtze Fleet's Monteno Kaiser ship, shot and killed the coolie Gu Qinggong (transliteration) in self-defense at 0:15 a.m. this morning (23rd). After the Special District Court sent personnel to examine the body, Qiu Fushi was exempted from criminal responsibility because he did not intentionally kill anyone. He was released together with the nine coolies present. However, Gu A'er, the brother of the deceased, refused to accept the pension and claimed that he would file a lawsuit with the American Inspector's Office. It is expected that this case may not avoid a legal battle. As for the content of this case, both sides have different opinions. When the body was examined this morning, Western detective Bai Lake testified that he suddenly heard the sound of a police whistle when patrolling Fair Road last night. He went to inquire and caught a glimpse of a Westerner with a pistol in his hand in the window of the dormitory at 15 Fair Road. Three other Chinese were crouching on the wall corner outside the window. When he entered the house to check, Gu Qinggong had died in the back room. After inquiring, he learned that the house was being repaired and the deceased was guarding the materials with several workers and living in the back room. Then, in the neighboring bathroom, he found a .45 caliber automatic pistol. He then took the Westerner Qiu Fushi and the nine coolies present back to the police station. One of the coolies was a cook hired by 8 Fair Road. Later, Qiu Fushi confessed that he was 30 years old and did not really intend to kill the deceased. It was only because the coolies wanted to attack him, so he fired into the air to scare them. It was not until the Western detective arrived that he learned that Gu had been shot and killed. The incident occurred at about 0:15 a.m. He was in dreamland when he was suddenly awakened by his wife, who said that someone had entered the room. He still thought that his wife was hallucinating due to excessive shock. Just as he was about to comfort her, the light of a flashlight shone on the bed. He jumped up from the bed, and the intruder fled to the back room. Behind his room door, he returned to the bedroom to get a pistol. The gun was brought from the United States five years ago, and he did not get a license because it was not used often. When he took the gun in his hand and was about to call the police, he heard the coolies trying to pry open the door to the neighboring bathroom. He then turned to another passage in the back of the room and saw that the door was half open. A coolie was standing behind the door with a giant stick, apparently waiting for him to pass by before attacking him. He then fired a shot into the air, intending to call the police. When the police arrived, they saw that the coolie had died. The bullet penetrated the door and hit his left jaw, etc. However, according to Chen Guiqing, a coolie present, it was different, saying that how dare the coolies attack a foreign sailor for no reason. In fact, it was because everyone was chatting around 11 p.m. last night when a child entered the room. Everyone drove him out. The child took the ladder and left, preventing everyone from going downstairs, because the stairs had been dismantled at that time. There was no way to go downstairs without the ladder. At 12:15, the worker surnamed Gu wanted to go to the bathroom and planned to pass through Qiu Fushi's bedroom to reach the front stairs. The sailor woke up, furious, and started beating the workers. While the workers were fleeing, Gu wanted to close the door, but Qiu shot and killed him. Finally, the coroner said that after inquiring about this case, Qiu Fushi did not intentionally shoot and kill. Now the deceased's family has a widow, a ten-year-old daughter, and a four-year-old son, who are poor and helpless. It is better to give them a pension and settle the matter peacefully. He then turned to ask Lieutenant Colonel Howard of the American warship how much the American Navy planned to give as a pension. He said that he wanted to know first whether these coolies were allowed to live upstairs and break into Qiu's room. At that time, the brother of the deceased claimed that he did not want to accept the pension and demanded that the person who opened fire and committed the crime be punished. The coroner then advised that the family of the deceased had two options: either file a lawsuit with the American Inspector's Office, or agree on a pension and settle the case through both parties. The remains are allowed to be claimed by the family for coffin burial. According to reports, Qiu Fushi rented the place with his wife in February. He first lived downstairs, but moved upstairs yesterday due to repairs. The pistol was his personal property and has been taken away by him along with the bullets.

The Public Concession 183

The Question of Female Patrol Officers

A Meeting Will Be Held to Decide After Talking with Johnson

The Shanghai Women's Organizations Joint Committee recently wrote to the Public Works Department, requesting the employment of female patrol officers in the concession. Later, the Public Works Department replied that the time was not yet appropriate. Recently, the committee responded to the request of the Police Committee and recommended representatives Ms. Elton and Ms. Smith to participate in the police meeting, so as to continue to state their opinions on the issue. After Ms. Elton attended the meeting, she deeply regretted that Mr. Johnson, a travel commissioner of the League of Nations, was suddenly ill and could not attend the meeting, because he had expertise in this issue. The chairman said that the Police Superintendent had visited the members of the travel group and discussed everything. After consultation between the Public Works Department and the Superintendent, it was decided to postpone the issue of employing female patrol officers until Major Jollard returned to Shanghai from England, and then consider it again. Then, at the request of the chairman, the two ladies stated their opinions on why female patrol officers must be prepared in the concession, mainly stating that female patrol officers in Western countries all patrol the streets, but the situation in Shanghai is different, and it is not convenient for them to be assigned to street patrols. Female patrol officers in Shanghai should manage the taking of confessions and inspections of those who commit crimes against children and women, and women who engage in improper behavior on the road, because it is difficult for men to do these things. The women mentioned by the two representatives specifically refer to foreigners. The two representatives then asked the Public Works Department whether it could first invite a foreign female police expert to investigate whether the situation in Shanghai is suitable for female patrol officers. If it is suitable, the Public Works Department can first hire a foreign female patrol officer, and then consider the situation to hire more to deal with Chinese women committing crimes. After the two representatives stated their opinions, the members of the Police Committee said that the various points stated were either without a solution, or if they were to be hired, they could not be effective with just three or five people. The Public Works Department really does not have the financial resources to maintain this. Then the two representatives asked the chairman to allow Johnson to meet within the next week, so as to continue to make suggestions. The chairman agreed, and everything will be decided at a meeting after talking with Johnson.

A Beautiful Woman Throws Herself into the River 184

The Auntie Spoke Sadly

Her Husband Went to Jail for Committing a Crime

The Mother-in-Law and Daughter-in-Law Slept Together Under One Quilt

The Daughter-in-Law Wanted to Remarry, But It Was Not Allowed

So She Had No Choice But to End It All

At around 6 p.m. the night before, a beautiful young woman in a cheongsam went to the Bund Wharf on Jiujiang Road alone, hailed a No. 106 sampan, and said that she would cross to Pudong. At that time, she paid 33 copper coins for the fare. When the sampan rocked to the center of the river, the young woman suddenly jumped into the river and committed suicide. Her body sank and floated again. Xin Shunlai, the sampanman, was shocked to see this and immediately used a bamboo pole to hook her clothes to save her. When asked why she jumped into the river, the young woman remained silent and only wept. Xin then sent her to the water patrol station and took dry clothes for her to change temporarily. After changing, she confessed that her name was Chen Aju, 18 years old, from Ninghai, Zhejiang. She lived at No. 257 Jinghe Lane, opposite Xuedou Temple, Xinjibang Road. She married Hu Tianyou, a fellow villager, at the age of 15. Her husband used to work as a steward on a Yi Tai Company ship, and his monthly salary was still abundant. At the end of the year before last, he was arrested by the Huishan Patrol Station in Tilanqiao for privately selling pistols and handed over to the court, which sentenced him to seven years in prison. He is still detained in prison and will not be released for another four or five years, resulting in the termination of the family's livelihood and extreme poverty. Last year, I gave birth to a daughter, who was sent by my mother-in-law to other people to raise. Now, because it is difficult to make a living, I am seeking death by throwing myself into the river. The head of the patrol temporarily ordered her to stay at the patrol station for one night. Yesterday morning, Detective Cheng Yongnian was sent to summon her aunt and explain the situation. Her aunt went to the patrol station weeping and confessed a tragic family situation. She said that her surname was Hu Guo, and she had two sons. The eldest son died of illness in March last year, leaving behind two children, seven and four years old. The eldest daughter-in-law suffered this great disaster and cried all day long, repeatedly holding the idea of seeking death. On January 30 of this year, she also died in her hometown. So I sent the two grandchildren to my aunt's house for safekeeping. Recently, because of the death of the eldest daughter-in-law, I took a wheel back to my hometown once to inquire and learned that my aunt had abused my two grandchildren. The older one was given a bowl of rice every day, and the younger one was given half a bowl, so they were so hungry that their faces were yellow and skinny. Later, I secretly took rice for the two grandchildren to eat, which caused a quarrel with my aunt. I returned to Shanghai in anger and found that the second daughter-in-law was missing. It turned out that last year, the second son, Tianyou, was imprisoned for selling pistols. Last year, the eldest son died, and the family was extremely poor. Only my second daughter-in-law Chen (i.e., the one who threw herself into the river) and I live in Shanghai. There is only one quilt on the bed, and the two of us sleep together. Chen wears a cheongsam outside now, and she only has one shirt. She washes it every time she is about to go to bed, and wears it again the next day after it is dry. This kind of life cannot be described in words. At this point, she burst into tears. Chen often went out because she could not bear the suffering. Last year, she gave birth to a daughter and refused to give her milk. I thought she would starve to death, but I couldn't bear it, so I sent her to other people to raise. Recently, when I returned to Shanghai from my hometown, Chen was not at home again. After many inquiries, I learned that she had an affair with a Mr. Yao, an employee of a tobacco company. However, Yao earns only 40 or 50 yuan a month, and he already has a wife at home. Chen is willing to be a concubine. Recently, she asked me in person to agree. I was angry when I heard this and answered that although your husband is in jail for committing a crime, he will eventually be released in four or five years. Although it is hard now, there will be a day for a comeback in the future, etc. Chen saw that I insisted on not agreeing, presumably the matter was hopeless, and she was unwilling to live this hard life at home, so she committed suicide without telling anyone. The staff of the patrol station sighed after hearing this. The head of the patrol ordered Guo to take her daughter-in-law back and persuade her to avoid repeating the same path.

A Female Corpse in the Quilt 185

A Man and a Woman Checked In, One Died and One Escaped

The Woman Was Lying Stiffly in the Quilt, Seemingly Strangled to Death

At around 2:45 p.m. the day before, a man and a woman came to the Sanjiang Hotel at 12 Beihai Road. The man was wearing a gray coat and a cap, speaking with a Songjiang accent. The woman was about 25 years old, wearing a camel-hair short jacket, with short hair and not very beautiful. The man spoke with the same accent as the man. The man first told the front desk that his surname was Wang, his name was Quanlong, 27 years old, from Songjiang, and the woman's surname was Zhu. The waiter led them to Room 33 upstairs to rest. The two of them drank some tea in the room. At around 4 p.m., they went out together, and before leaving, they ordered the waiter to change their names at the front desk. So, it was noted in the circulation book that the man was Wang Desheng, and the woman was Zhang. At 11 p.m. that night, the two of them came back, closed the door, and went to sleep. At 7 a.m. yesterday morning, Wang got up first and went out alone, and told the waiter not to disturb the female guest and let her sleep peacefully. After speaking, he left. At 9 a.m., a Lu Ruisheng came to visit Wang Desheng. Because Wang was not there, he left a name card and left. At noon, the waiter wanted to ask the female guest whether she wanted to continue the room. He shouted outside the door several times, but there was no reply. So he pried open the door and entered. The room was silent. The bedding on the bed was piled high. The female guest surnamed Zhang was lying in the middle. When he uncovered the quilt, the woman was dead. She was lying stiffly on her side, facing inward. There was a silk trouser belt around her neck. She was strangled to death. When he looked again, there was also some blood on her mouth. He immediately reported to the patrol station, which sent detectives to investigate. In addition to taking the clothes left behind back to the patrol station, the doctor also examined the female corpse. At the same time, detectives were sent to Fengjing and other places to investigate the escaped Wang Desheng.

Prohibition 186

Marriage Introduction Agencies

Beautifully Named Marriage Research Association

Municipal Government Sends Letter to French Consulate to Strictly Ban Them

The Municipal Government yesterday, in order to ban marriage introduction agencies, specially sent a letter to French Consul General Koechlin, to swiftly and strictly ban them in order to maintain public morals and avoid causing harm to society. The original letter stated: "Regarding the matter approved by the Ministry of Interior, Document No. 36, concerning the instruction of affairs: According to a report in the *Shanghai Sun* newspaper on March 9th, in a certain lane on Avenue Joffre in the French Concession of Shanghai, there is a marriage introduction agency called the Marriage Research Association. Although it has not been registered, it is working hard and has introduced many men and women who have become married couples. The person in charge is a certain Tao, etc. After investigating marriage introduction agencies, Zhang Junlin, a citizen of this capital, submitted a request to establish one, asking for prior registration, etc. The ministry responded by saying that in our country, marriage has always valued the words of matchmakers, as a way to unite two surnames and to begin proper human relations. Historically, matchmakers have always been relatives and old friends. We have never heard of matchmaking as a profession, likening people to horse traders. As for the official matchmaker established in the Rites of Zhou, they were in charge of national laws and regulations, and their duties were like today's registration. The government has its own plans for unified management, which cannot be imitated by the people. Moreover, the current principle is that men and women determine their own engagements. How can one seize a passerby to advise them and make them responsible for introductions? The proposal to organize a marriage introduction agency so that single men and women can all become good couples is contrary to ancient customs and new systems and is like trying to fit a square peg in a round hole. It is not suitable for our national conditions and may lead to bad customs. The request is not approved, and a special rejection is issued. Zhang Junlin's original submission mentioned that Shanghai already had such organizations, so the report in the newspaper seems to be based on fact. However, it is a stain that the French Concession allows the establishment of such illegal places, and methods should be devised to ban them in order to rectify morals and avoid providing excuses. Accordingly, we request that you investigate and handle this matter according to the law and that you provide a response." Based on this, on October 30th of last year, we received a letter from the Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Nationalist Party, stating that the "Chinese National Seven Rights Marriage Election Association" was established at No. 48, Lane 1, Baoyu Lane, Dongxin Bridge, French Concession, with absurd content and should be banned. We then sent a letter to your Consul General requesting that the ban be enforced. Later, on November 14th of the same year, we received a reply stating that the police had been instructed to investigate. According to the reply, two people had lived there in July, claiming to be members of the association, but they were not seen receiving outsiders or holding meetings, etc., and they moved away in early September, and their whereabouts are unknown. Now, according to the *Shanghai Sun* newspaper, there is a marriage introduction agency called the Marriage Research Association in a certain lane on Avenue Joffre. It is not known whether this is a disguised form of the previous Election Association. However, any similar organization is harmful to public morals and should be strictly banned to avoid causing harm to society. In addition to the reply, we are sending this letter, hoping that you will investigate and instruct for a strict ban and that you will provide a response. Addressed to Koechlin, French Consul General in Shanghai.

Lizhong Lane 191

Tenants Resist Landlord's Rent Increase

According to the Guomin News Agency, all 140 households of tenants in Lizhong Lane at the end of Yuezhou Road and Feihong Road in Hongzhen in this city are resisting an illegal rent increase and unreasonable oppression by the landlord, Chen Changkun. The tenants held a reception for the press of this city at the Pacific Western Restaurant the night before last, attended by more than ten people. During the reception, representatives of the tenants reported that in January of last year, the landlord suddenly announced a rent increase to the tenants under the pretext of the Finance Bureau collecting a 14% housing tax. After repeated negotiations, the result was that stone-framed doors and shop houses would be increased by one dollar, and Cantonese-style houses would be increased by half a dollar, starting from April of the 19th year of the Republic. The rental agent, Ju Kangzhuang, formally agreed in writing that the rent would not be increased again for three years. Unexpectedly, after only eight months, Ju Kangzhuang transferred the rental to the Huada Foreign Firm, which arbitrarily set various harsh conditions and laid off two gatekeepers and patrolmen, resulting in two robberies and one assassination in the lane within a week. Unexpectedly, the landlord continued to act recklessly, again transferring the rental of the houses to the China Business Company. The conditions set were even more harsh than when the Huada Foreign Firm was the rental agent, and it was announced that the rent would be increased by 30% from February 1st. The tenants could no longer tolerate this and began to unite to oppose it, requesting that justice be upheld and assistance be provided. It is also heard that the tenants have now formally filed a lawsuit to seek a legal solution. It is reported that the local court has notified both parties to appear in court for trial on the 28th.

Establishment of the Huaxin Lane Tenants' Association 192

Huaxin Lane on Yangshupu Road in this city has newly built houses. The houses are owned by the wealthy Sheng family and rented out by the Huizhong Banking Corporation. Most of the tenants are workers from nearby factories. The company suddenly announced to all tenants that the rent would be increased by 50% per house in the market (from the original rent of 24 yuan to 36 yuan) and by 40% per room in the lane (from the original rent of 15.2 yuan to 21.2 yuan) under the pretext of increasing water supply. The tenants were all shocked and sent letters requesting that the order to increase the rent be withdrawn. The company ignored them all. The tenants then organized a Tenants' Association to seek a solution. Yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, they held an inaugural meeting, electing Wang Weichuan, Lu Jianyun, Wu Tingzhen, Jin Zhengjiang, Xu Yonglin, Zhang Xueshu, Wang Songtao, Fang A'ming, Chen Longbao, Ding Yongtai, Peng Debiao, Ge Laosi, Hu Junjie, Zheng Juenong, Diao Xiuzhang, Yu Afu, Yuan Xinchen, Lu Fengming, Bian Yongchao, Wang Fuzeng, Qi Huaizhang, and 21 others as executive committee members. They immediately took their oaths of office and chose to begin work tomorrow (i.e., today), assigning duties and submitting a report for the record.

Qinglian Pavilion Caught in the Middle 193

Landlord Sues for Eviction

Tenants Refuse to Vacate

The houses of Qinglian Pavilion on Fourth Horse Road originally belonged to the New Sassoon Company. Last autumn, New Sassoon sold the property to the Sanyuan Real Estate Company. The 25-year lease agreement between Qinglian Pavilion and New Sassoon was about to expire, so Sanyuan notified Qinglian Pavilion that it should be vacated on the expiration date. However, the shops on the ground floor of Qinglian Pavilion are all subleased from Qinglian Pavilion and requested an extension, which Sanyuan refused. As a result, Qinglian Pavilion is in a difficult position, having to deal with the tenants and the landlord. Therefore, it retained lawyer Shen Yuesheng to file a lawsuit with the Special District Local Court, requesting a judgment ordering the tenants to vacate so that the house could be returned to the landlord. The landlord also retained a lawyer to file a lawsuit against Qinglian Pavilion for eviction. The Special Court held a preliminary hearing for mediation, but no agreement was reached, and a formal summons will be issued in the coming days.

Record of the Trial of the Kidnapping of Qu Chengqing 194

Qu Attends Court in Person to Testify

Claims He Was Rescued Without Spending a Penny

Qu Chengqing, an employee of a foreign firm, was kidnapped on Haining Road in January of last year. Subsequently, the police rescued Qu from the bandit's den and captured several kidnappers, who were all interrogated and punished by the Special District Local Court. Recently, Shi Arong, the ringleader of the case, was captured and detained for interrogation. This has been reported in previous news. The trial continued yesterday morning. Qu Chengqing and Luo Zhu, the landlady of the two rooms at No. 1548, Runde Lane, Gongping Road, where the hostage was hidden, were summoned to court to testify. Qu first described the kidnapping, stating that on the night of January 11th, he was returning home from outside and had reached the entrance of his residence at No. 1760 Haining Road when six kidnappers suddenly arrived, two of them holding pistols. They forced him into a car prepared by the bandits and drove him to the bandit's den, where he was hidden upstairs. They immediately forced him to write a letter to his family, demanding 100,000 yuan ransom.

Page 16

He stayed for about a week and was rescued. He did not spend a penny. He did not know whether the defendant was the ringleader. Next, Luo Zhu testified that Shi Arong and another person had come to rent the upstairs room. Later, a woman and a child came to live with them. The woman was Shi's wife. It was said that Shi opened a car dealership on Dengtu Road. They lived there for about a week. The woman and child left, and Shi said that he had returned to his hometown. Later, the hostage was brought to my house, and I really didn't know, etc. When questioned, Shi Arong denied being a bandit. Judge Feng ordered that he be detained for a continued hearing at a later date.

Yang Da Stabbed to Death by Enemies 195

Yang Da, a man from Jiangbei in his twenties, lived in a thatched shed in the lane east of the Silk Factory on Singapore Road in western Shanghai. He was usually restless, resulting in feuds with others outside. On the night before last, Yang had already gone to bed when he was suddenly attacked by several enemies, armed with sharp knives and iron rods, who stabbed Yang's body and head more than ten times, killing him on the spot. After his death, the body was dragged outside the door, and an iron rod was tied to his body. The murderers fled the scene. When the Sixth District Police Station learned of this, they ordered an arrest, but were unsuccessful. Yesterday, they ordered Tan Hefu, the head of the 89th Tu, to report the matter to the Local Court. Prosecutor Wang and other inspectors were commissioned to inspect the scene and confirmed that he had been killed. The family was ordered to collect the body and await the arrest of the murderers. The iron rod was taken to the court for storage.

Traveler Dies from Suicide 197

Related to Marital Discord and Economic Pressure

On the 19th of this month, a traveler came to the Yingbin Hotel in Qinghe Lane, Zhejiang Road, claiming to be surnamed Zheng, named Wenpin, from Ningbo, and coming from Hankou. He stayed in room 214. Around 9:00 PM the night before last, he suddenly committed suicide by ingesting opium in his room. He was discovered and rushed to the Tongren Hospital for treatment, but it was too late. He died in the hospital at 2:00 AM yesterday morning. According to those who knew Zheng, his actions were due to both marital discord and economic pressure. Zheng was 27 years old and worked at the Yihe Tai Wood Shop at the racecourse entrance in the Special District of Hankou. Recently, he was engaged to Guo Yulian of the Zheng Shunfeng Wood Shop through the introduction of a friend. However, the woman's mother disapproved of the marriage because Zheng had no permanent property and was far away in another province, and she instructed her daughter to write a letter to Zheng, canceling the previous agreement. It is possible that this led to his rash decision, etc.

China Harmonica Society to Perform in Beijing 198

The China Harmonica Society at No. 168, Sichuan Road, Beijing Road in this city has become famous since its establishment. Recently, it was invited by the Nanjing Central Radio Station to broadcast in Beijing. All 32 male and female members of the society's harmonica team are scheduled to depart on the night express on May 1st, led by President Wang Qingxun. After the broadcast, they will also hold a separate "Harmonica Concert" at 7:30 PM on the evening of the 2nd at the auditorium of Jinling University on Drum Tower to allow people in the capital to enjoy it. It is also heard that they will be invited by the National Assembly to participate in entertainment events. In addition, in order to popularize this folk music, the society will continue to recruit new members in May, with primary classes and "noon special classes." The teaching is serious and the membership fee is very low. People from all walks of life, whether beginners or experienced, are welcome to join. Brochures are available for collection.

Traditional Chinese Medicine Practitioner He Lisan Discusses Preventing Seasonal Diseases 199

Dr. He Lisan, a traditional Chinese medicine practitioner at Wang Yi Ma Lane, diagonally opposite Shenxiang Pavilion inside the New North Gate, is a top student of the late famous doctor Jin Baichuan. He has special insights into the treatment of typhoid fever and various pediatric diseases. Dr. He said that recently the weather has been abnormal, and seasonal diseases are prevalent. There are many cases of meningitis and measles, especially among children. The methods of prevention include vaccination, paying attention to diet and temperature, and decocting one fresh reed root (with nodes removed), three qian of Chuzhou chrysanthemum, and seven water chestnuts daily as a tea substitute to avoid infection. Children are of pure yang constitution and tend to have internal heat and phlegm. Reed root can clear heat, Chuzhou chrysanthemum can soothe the liver and extinguish wind, and water chestnuts can dissolve phlegm and reduce stagnation. If there is no accumulation inside, seasonal evils will not be able to invade. Even if they are affected, the condition will be mild. Those who are already affected should still seek medical treatment. Dr. He is now willing to serve as a social medical consultant. If patients encounter difficult and complicated diseases, they can write to Dr. He's residence to discuss treatment methods, and he will provide detailed answers.

Lost Boy Ma Xiaolong Awaiting Collection 200

The Municipal Public Security Bureau received a lost boy named Ma Xiaolong yesterday, sent by the Second District. He claimed to be 14 years old, from Danyang, and living in Danyang Lingdi Fang. His father's name is Ma Sancheng, a mason. I came to Shanghai with my father three years ago to apprentice as a carpenter at the Dongyang Company Wharf. My master's name is Zhen Ming. Because I didn't want to apprentice at the carpenter shop, I secretly ran away last month and apprenticed at a porridge shop. Yesterday, I went out to play and lost my way, etc. The boy has a shaved head and is wearing a black cloth jacket and pants, a black cotton vest, patterned socks, and rubber overshoes. He was sent to the Women and Children Relief Association for care and a notice was placed in the newspaper to find his family.

Weather Report 201

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that the coastal areas here may have cloudy and rainy weather with heavy fog. The Yangtze River basin has low barometric pressure. The wind on the Yellow Sea is coming from the east to the southeast. The mouth of the Yangtze River has a south wind, and the Taiwan Strait has a northeast wind. Also, the highest temperature in this city in the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday was 64.4 degrees, and the lowest was 50.0 degrees. The highest temperature on the same day last year was 86.7 degrees, and the lowest was 62.2 degrees.

Youth Land

The Bell Society of Jiangnan College 202

Jiangnan College on Connaught Road, Jin Situ Temple Street, has been very crowded with students this semester. The students are all working very hard on extracurricular academic research. Several organizations, such as the Qingdao Society and the Social Science Research Association, have been established one after another. Recently, the Bell Society has been organized, with the pure purpose of studying social sciences, natural sciences, and literature and art. Therefore, many students have participated. The society held its inaugural meeting yesterday and elected Jin Caiqiao, Shao Rongjiu, Jiang Zixun, and 25 others as executive committee members, and Ying Yao and seven others as alternate executive committee members. They plan to publish a weekly publication and prepare to publish a special publication on academic research. They also plan to invite famous people to give lectures every week to encourage each other.

Night Patrol 203

— A Moment

It was as if in a dream, the fine rain outside the window gently tapping the leaves, a poetic clear sound filling the dark night. Suddenly, the sound of an iron rod hitting a stone, "jiji," startled me awake from my hazy memory. I lazily opened my sleepy eyes and saw that the dark house was suddenly filled with unexpected light. "Ah, isn't that the brilliance of a flashlight?" I muttered to myself.

Anyone would find it strange and shocking that someone would shine a flashlight outside the window and make the sound of iron tools at this late hour. A kind of inexplicable terror tightened around me. So I quickly put on my vest and got up.

"Min, wake up, wake up, something's happening..."

I asked Mr. Wu in the room, but my throat felt a little unnatural.

"What... what..." he asked in alarm.

"Didn't you hear the sound of an iron rod dragging outside just now?"

"What, an iron rod?"

"Yes, an iron rod, and a flashlight is shining everywhere. Get up and see what's going on."

"I'm afraid, Lao Zhang... just now in my dream I saw a bloody corpse in a wheat field. Tonight's unfortunate change may be a foreboding of my dream."

"What's there to be afraid of? We didn't kill anyone's parents. Get up, be brave."

Mr. Wu couldn't resist my urging, so he put on his coat. We each carried a kind of fearful and mysterious thought, waiting for something unfortunate to happen.

The darkness all around was a little frightening. All the sounds were swallowed by the god of night. Only the gentle breeze kissing the willow branches made a delicate whisper rippling in the lonely air. Mr. Wu and I searched around the dormitory in silence, peering as if looking for something precious.

"Look, isn't there a dark shadow approaching us in front?"

I said to Mr. Wu in a low voice.

"Yes, yes, so what do we do?" He seemed a little scared.

"We'll go forward and ask to find out what's going on."

"......................"

"Who?" It was the voices of the Misses asking, followed by the shining of a flashlight.

"Me, me," we quickly walked towards them.

"Miss Chen, Miss Wang... what are you looking for? It's so late," I asked.

"Quietly, Mr. Zhang, tonight there are troublemakers who want to burn us to death..."

"Last night we found a lot of straw and cotton paper soaked in kerosene. Tonight we found a lot too. If we don't sacrifice our sleep, maybe all the students will be burned to death by these ruthless troublemakers," Miss Chen was interrupted by Miss Li, who was usually good at eloquence, before she could finish speaking.

"So, where did you get this news?" I asked suspiciously.

"The other day, a few boxes of bees were placed next to your male dormitory, weren't they burned for no reason? At that time, we all went to dinner, so we didn't know who did it. Later, we heard that a few bad people wanted to burn down all the houses. Therefore, we all have to be careful and pay attention," Miss Chen said angrily.

"Just a few of you, aren't you afraid?" Mr. Wu said.

"What are we afraid of? What we're afraid of is not being able to see them! Those troublemakers," Miss Li said.

"You don't sleep all night? That's really too hard," I asked worriedly.

"We have to patrol all night, but in two shifts, one for the first half of the night and one for the second half of the night, with eight or nine people in each shift. You male students are the same," Miss Li replied.

"Okay, continue your work, but be careful of unexpected misfortunes."

"Thank you," they said as they went to do their work.

Each of them was very brave and patrolled everywhere. Some held wooden sticks, some held iron rods, and some held flashlights. The color on their faces was still rosy, without a trace of fear.

Youth Land Submission Guidelines 204

(1) The text should be about discussions on youth issues, news about domestic and foreign schools or students, essays, descriptions of school life, random notes, etc. The style is not limited.

(2) The drawings are limited to those related to youth issues.

(3) Photos are qualified if they are about youth life (such as sports, travel, sightseeing, theater performances, lectures, gatherings, exhibitions, various competitions, etc.), school news, and youth movements, etc. Individuals and groups are welcome.

(4) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not use blue ink to draw attachments in the manuscript, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.
